ADOPTING ORDINANCE
Ordinance Number 10-1999
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE CITY OF ROCHESTER, INDIANA AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY.
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the first supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Political
Subdivision, which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and
permanent nature enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances
of this Political Subdivision; and
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision or
addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make reference to sections of the Indiana code; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Legislative Authority to accept these updated
sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of Indiana; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE LEGISLATIVE AUTHORITY OF THE POLITICAL
SUBDIVISION OF THE CITY OF ROCHESTER, INDIANA:
Section 1. That the first supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Political
Subdivision as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of
Cincinnati, Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by
reference as if set out in its entirety.
Section 2.Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the day of its
adoption and approval by the Legislative Authority and the Clerk of the
Political Subdivision is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such
supplement into the copy of the Code of Ordinances kept on file in the Office
of the Clerk.
Section 3.This ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary for
the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare of
the people of this municipality.
Section 4: That this ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after
its passage as provided by law and the filing thereof in the Office of the
Clerk-Treasurer.
Passed by the Common Council of the City of Rochester, Fulton County, Indiana,
this 13th day,
April, 1999.

ORDINANCE NO. 08-2013
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE CITY OF ROCHESTER AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 2013 S-6 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Political
Subdivision, which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and
permanent nature enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances
of this Political Subdivision; and
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision or
addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make references to sections of the Indiana code; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Legislative Authority to accept these updated
sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of Indiana; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED by the Common Council of the City of Rochester as
follows:
Section l.   That the 2013 S-6 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the
Political Subdivision as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of
Cincinnati, Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by
reference as if set out in its entirety.
Section 2.   Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the day of its
adoption and approval by the Legislative Authority and the Clerk of the
Political Subdivision is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such
supplement into the copy of the Code of Ordinances kept on file in the Office
of the Clerk.
Section 3.   This ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary
for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare
of the people of this municipality, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
Passed by the Common Council of Rochester, Indiana the 24th day of September
2013.

WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,

for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare

ORDINANCE NO. 04-2017
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE CITY OF ROCHESTER
AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 2017 S-8 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Political
Subdivision, which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and
permanent nature enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances
of this Political Subdivision; and
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision or
addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make references to sections of the Indiana code; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Legislative Authority to accept these updated
sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of Indiana; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED by the Common Council of the City of Rochester as
follows:
      Section 1.   That the 2017 S-8 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of
the Political Subdivision as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation
of Cincinnati, Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted
by reference as if set out in its entirety.
      Section 2.   Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the day of
its adoption and approval by the Legislative Authority and the Clerk of the
Political Subdivision is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such
supplement into the copy of the Code of Ordinances kept on file in the Office
of the Clerk-Treasurer.
      Section 3.   This ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure
necessary for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and
general welfare of the people of this municipality, and shall take effect at
the earliest date provided by law.
Passed by the Common Council of Rochester, Indiana the 22nd day of August 2017.

ORDINANCE NO. 06-2019
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE CITY OF ROCHESTER AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 2019 S-10 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Political
Subdivision, which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and
permanent nature enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances
of this Political Subdivision; and
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision or
addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make references to sections of the Indiana code; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Legislative Authority to accept these updated
sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of Indiana; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED by the Common Council of the City of Rochester as
follows:
Section 1.   That the 2019 S-10 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the
Political Subdivision as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of
Cincinnati, Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by

Section 3.   This ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary
for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare
of the people of this municipality, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
Passed by the Common Council of Rochester, Indiana the 27th day of August,
2019.

§ 10.01 TITLE OF CODE.
   This codification of ordinances by and for the city of Rochester, Indiana
shall be designated as the Code of Rochester Indiana and may be so cited.
§ 10.02 INTERPRETATION.
   (A)   Unless otherwise provided herein, or by law or implication required,
the same rules of construction, definition, and application shall govern the
interpretation of this code as those governing the interpretation of state law.
   (B)   All general provisions, terms, phrases and expressions contained in
this code shall be liberally construed in order that the true intent and
meaning of the Common Council may be fully carried out.
   (C)   In the interpretation and application of any provisions of this code,
they shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted for the promotion of
the public health, safety, comfort, convenience and general welfare. Where any
provision of this code imposes greater restrictions upon the subject matter
than another more general provision imposed by the code or other law, the
provision imposing the greater restriction or regulation shall be deemed to be
controlling.
('79 Code, § 1-2)
§ 10.03 APPLICATION TO FUTURE ORDINANCES.
   All provisions of Title I compatible with future legislation, shall apply to
ordinances hereafter adopted amending or supplementing this code unless
otherwise specifically provided.
§ 10.04 CAPTIONS.
   Headings and captions used in this code other than the title, chapter, and
section numbers are employed for reference purposes only and shall not be
deemed a part of the text of any section.
§ 10.05 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   General rule. Words and phrases shall be taken in their plain, or
ordinary and usual sense. However, technical words and phrases having a
peculiar and appropriate meaning in law shall be understood according to their
technical import.
   (B)   For the purpose of this code, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CITY, MUNICIPAL CORPORATION, or MUNICIPALITY. The City of Rochester,
Indiana.
   COMMON COUNCIL or COUNCIL. The Common Council of the City of Rochester.
   CODE, THIS CODE or THIS CODE OF ORDINANCES. This City Code of Rochester
Indiana as modified by amendment, revision, and adoption of new titles,
chapters, or sections.
   COMPUTATION OF TIME. In computing any period of time prescribed or allowed
by this code of ordinances, by order of the court, or by any applicable
ordinance or statute, the day of the act, event, or default from which the
designated period of time begins to run shall not be included. The last day of
the period so computed is to be included unless it is: a Saturday; a Sunday; a
legal holiday as defined by state statute; or a day the office in which the act
is to be done is closed during regular business hours. In any event, the period
runs until the end of the next day that is not a Saturday, a Sunday, a legal
holiday, or a day on which the office is closed. When the period of time
allowed is less than seven days, intermediate Saturdays, Sundays, legal
holidays, and days on which the office is closed shall be excluded from the
computation.
(Indiana Rules of Trial Procedure, Rule 6(A))
   CORPORATE LIMITS, CITY LIMITS. The legal boundaries of the City of
Rochester, except as otherwise provided by law.
   COUNTY. Fulton County, Indiana.
   JOINT AUTHORITY. All words giving joint authority to three or more persons
or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such
persons or officers.
   MAY. The act referred to is permissive.
   MAYOR. The Mayor of the City of Rochester.
   MONTH. A calendar month.
   NUMBER. A word importing the singular number only may extend and be applied
to several persons and things as well as to one person and thing, and a word
importing the plural may extend to the singular.
   OATH. An affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be
substituted for an oath, and in such cases the words SWEAR and SWORN shall be
equivalent to the words AFFIRM and AFFIRMED.
   OFFICER, OFFICE, EMPLOYEE, COMMISSION, or DEPARTMENT. An officer, office,
employee, commission, or department of this city unless the context clearly
requires otherwise.
   OWNER. Any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, tenant in partnership,
joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety of the whole or of a part of such
building or land.
   PERSON. Extends and applies to associations, clubs, societies, firms,
partnerships, bodies politic and corporate or any other group acting as a unit
as well to natural persons.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY. Includes every species of property except real property,
as herein described.
   PRECEDING or FOLLOWING. Next before or next after, respectively.
   PROPERTY. Shall include real and personal property.
   PUBLIC PLACE. Any street or highway, sidewalk, park, cemetery, school yard
or open space adjacent thereto and any lake or stream.
   QUORUM. A majority of the members of a board, commission or committee
holding office, unless otherwise specifically provided in this code.
   REAL PROPERTY. Shall include lands, tenements and hereditaments.
   SHALL. The act referred to is mandatory.
   SIDEWALK. Any portion of a street between the curbline and the adjacent
property line intended for the use of pedestrians, excluding parkways.
   SIGNATURE or SUBSCRIPTION. Includes a mark when the person cannot write.
   STATE. The State of Indiana.
   STREET. Shall be construed to embrace streets, avenues, boulevards, roads,
alleys, viaducts and all other public highways in the city.
   SUBCHAPTER. A division of a chapter, designated in this code by a heading in
the chapter analysis and a capitalized heading in the body of the chapter,
setting apart a group of sections related by the subject matter of the heading.
Not all chapters have subchapters.
   TENANT OR OCCUPANT. Shall include any person holding a written or oral lease
or who occupies the whole or a part of such building or land, either alone or
with others.
   WRITTEN. Any representation of words, letters, or figures, whether by
printing or otherwise.
   YEAR. A calendar year, unless otherwise expressed; equivalent to the words
YEAR OF OUR LORD.
('79 Code, § 1-2)
§ 10.06 RULES OF CONSTRUCTION.
   The construction of all ordinances of this city shall be by the following
rules, unless such construction is plainly repugnant to the intent of the
Common Council or of the context of the same ordinance:
   (A)    AND or OR. Either conjunction shall include the other as if written
“and/or,” if the sense requires it.
   (B)   Acts by assistants. When a statute or ordinance requires an act to be
done which, by law, an agent or deputy as well may do as the principal, such
requisition shall be satisfied by the performance of such act by an authorized
agent or deputy.
   (C)   Gender; singular and plural; tenses. Words denoting the masculine
gender shall be deemed to include the feminine and neuter genders; words in the
singular shall include the plural, and words in the plural shall include the
singular; the use of a verb in the present tense shall include the future, if
applicable.
   (D)   General term. A general term following specific enumeration of terms
is not to be limited to the class enumerated unless expressly so limited.
§ 10.07 SEVERABILITY.
   If any provision of this code as now or later amended or its application to
any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect
other provisions that can be given effect without the invalid provision or
application.
§ 10.08 REFERENCE TO OTHER SECTIONS.
   Whenever in one section reference is made to another section hereof, such
reference shall extend and apply to the section referred to as subsequently
amended, revised, recodified, or renumbered unless the subject matter is
changed or materially altered by the amendment or revision.
§ 10.09 REFERENCE TO OFFICES.
   Reference to a public office or officer shall be deemed to apply to any
office, officer, or employee of this city exercising the powers, duties, or
functions contemplated in the provision, irrespective of any transfer of
functions or change in the official title of the functionary.
§ 10.10 ERRORS AND OMISSIONS.
   If a manifest error is discovered, consisting of the misspelling of any
words; the omission of any word or words necessary to express the intention of
the provisions affected; the use of a word or words to which no meaning can be
attached; or the use of a word or words when another word or words was clearly
intended to express such intent, such spelling shall be corrected and such word
or words supplied, omitted, or substituted as will conform with the manifest
intention, and the provisions shall have the same effect as though the correct
words were contained in the text as originally published. No alteration shall
be made or permitted if any question exists regarding the nature or extent of
such error.
§ 10.11 OFFICIAL TIME.
   The official time, as established by applicable state/federal laws, shall be
the official time within this city for the transaction of all city business.
§ 10.12 REASONABLE TIME.
   In all cases where an ordinance requires an act to be done in a reasonable
time or requires reasonable notice to be given, reasonable time or notice shall
be deemed to mean the time which is necessary for a prompt performance of such
act or the giving of such notice.
§ 10.13 ORDINANCES REPEALED.
   This code, from and after its effective date, shall contain all of the
provisions of a general nature pertaining to the subjects herein enumerated and
embraced. All prior ordinances pertaining to the subjects treated by this code
shall be deemed repealed from and after the effective date of this code.
§ 10.14 ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature and all other ordinances
pertaining to subjects not embraced in this code shall remain in full force and
effect unless herein repealed expressly or by necessary implication.
§ 10.15 EFFECTIVE DATE OF ORDINANCES.
   All ordinances passed by the Common Council requiring publication shall take
effect from and after the due publication thereof, unless otherwise expressly
provided. Ordinances not requiring publication shall take effect from their
passage, unless otherwise expressly provided.
§ 10.16 REPEAL OR MODIFICATION OF ORDINANCE.
   (A)   Whenever any ordinance or part of an ordinance shall be repealed or
modified by a subsequent ordinance, the ordinance or part of an ordinance thus
repealed or modified shall continue in force until the due publication of the
ordinance repealing or modifying it when publication is required to give effect
thereto, unless otherwise expressly provided.
   (B)   No suit, proceedings, right, fine, forfeiture, or penalty instituted,
created, given, secured, or accrued under any ordinance previous to its repeal
shall in any way be affected, released, or discharged, but may be prosecuted,
enjoyed, and recovered as fully as if the ordinance had continued in force
unless it is otherwise expressly provided.
   (C)   When any ordinance repealing a former ordinance, clause, or provision
shall be itself repealed, the repeal shall not be construed to revive the
former ordinance, clause, or provision, unless it is expressly provided.
§ 10.17 ORDINANCES WHICH AMEND OR SUPPLEMENT CODE.
   (A)   If the Common Council shall desire to amend any existing chapter or
section of this code, the chapter or section shall be specifically repealed and
a new chapter or section, containing the desired amendment, substituted in its
place.
   (B)   Any ordinance which is proposed to add to the existing code a new
chapter or section shall indicate, with reference to the arrangement of this
code, the proper number of such chapter or section. In addition to such
indication thereof as may appear in the text of the proposed ordinance, a
caption or title shall be shown in concise form above the ordinance.
§ 10.18 SECTION HISTORIES; STATUTORY REFERENCES.
   (A)   If a section of this code is derived from the previous code of
ordinances of the city published in 1979 and subsequently amended, the 1979
code section number shall be indicated in the history by “('79 Code, §
       ).”
   (B)   As histories for the code sections, the specific number and passage
date of the original ordinance, and the most recent three amending ordinances,
if any, are listed following the text of the code section. Example: (Ord. 10,
passed 5-13-60; Am. Ord. 15, passed 1-1-70; Am. Ord. 20, passed 1-1-80; Am.
Ord. 25, passed 1-1-85)
   (C)   (1)   If a statutory cite is included in the history, this indicates
that the text of the section reads substantially the same as the statute.
Example: (I.C. 36-4-5-3) (Ord. 10, passed 1-17-80; Am. Ord. 20, passed 1-1-85).
      (2)   If a statutory cite is set forth as a “statutory reference”
following the text of the section, this indicates that the reader should refer
to that statute for further information. Example:
      § 39.01 PUBLIC RECORDS AVAILABLE.
         This municipality shall make available to any person for inspection or
copying all public records, unless otherwise exempted by state law.
      Statutory reference:
         For provisions concerning the inspection of public records, see I.C.
5-14-3-1 et seq.
§ 10.19 RECORDATION AND PUBLICATION OF ORDINANCES.
   (A)   The ordinances and resolutions adopted by the Common Council shall be
recorded by the Clerk-Treasurer in the minute books of the Council, and a copy
kept in an ordinance file. Due proof of publication of all ordinances requiring
publication together with the affidavit of the printer or publisher shall be
obtained by the Clerk-Treasurer and attached to the original of each ordinance
adopted by the Common Council in the minute book of the Council. ('79 Code, §
1-7)
   (B)   Within a reasonable time after an ordinance of the Common Council is
adopted, the Clerk-Treasurer shall record it in a book kept for that purpose.
The record must include: the signature of the Mayor; the attestation of the
Clerk-Treasurer; the Mayor's approval or veto of the ordinance; if applicable,
a memorandum of the passage of the ordinance over the veto; and the date of
each recorded item. The record or a certified copy of it constitutes
presumptive evidence of the adoption of the ordinance. (I.C. 36-4-6-17)
   (C)   (1)   An ordinance, order, or resolution passed by the Common Council
is considered adopted when it is: signed by the Mayor and either approved by
the Mayor or passed over his veto by the Council, under I.C. 36-4-6-16. If
required by statute, an adopted ordinance, order, or resolution must be
promulgated or published before it takes effect.
      (2)   An ordinance prescribing a penalty or forfeiture for a violation
must, before it takes effect, be published in a manner prescribed by I.C. 5-3-
1, unless it is published under division (C)(3) below, or there is an urgent
necessity requiring its immediate effectiveness, the Mayor proclaims the urgent
necessity, and copies of the ordinance are posted in three public places in
each of the districts from which members are elected to the Council.
      (3)   Except as provided in division (C)(5) below, if a city publishes
any of its ordinances in book or pamphlet form, no other publication is
required. If an ordinance prescribing a penalty or forfeiture for a violation
is published under this section, it takes effect two weeks after the
publication of the book or pamphlet. Publication under this subdivision, if
authorized by the Council, constitutes presumptive evidence of the ordinances
in the book or pamphlet, of the date of adoption of the ordinance, and that the
ordinances have been properly signed, attested, recorded and approved.
      (4)   This division (C) does not apply to a zoning ordinance or amendment
to a zoning ordinance, or a resolution approving a comprehensive plan, that is
adopted under I.C. 36-7
      (5)    An ordinance increasing a building permit fee on new development
must be published one time in accordance with I.C. 5-3-1 and not later than 30
days after the ordinance is adopted by the legislative body in accordance with
I.C. 5-3-1 and delay the implementation of the fee increase for 90 days after
the date the ordinance is published as provided above. (I.C. 36-4-6-14)
Statutory reference:
   Recording, publishing city ordinances, see I.C. and 36-4-6-17
§ 10.20 OFFENSES PUNISHABLE UNDER SEPARATE PROVISIONS.
   In all cases where the same offenses may be made punishable or may be
created by different clauses or sections of the ordinances of the city, the
prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed, but not more than one
recovery shall be had against the same person for the same offense.
('79 Code, § 1-12)
§ 10.21 OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES NOT TO BE PUNISHED.
   Except as specifically provided otherwise, no city officer or employee shall
be subject to fine or punishment under the provisions of this code for his
failure to do any act required by this code.
('79 Code, § 1-13)
§ 10.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   Wherever in this code or in any ordinance of the city, or rule or regulation
promulgated by an officer or agency thereof under the authority invested by law
or ordinance, any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an
offense, or the doing of any act is required, or the failure to do any act is
declared to be unlawful, where no specific penalty is provided therefor, the
violation of any such provision of this code, ordinance, rule or regulation is
declared to be a misdemeanor, and shall be punished by a fine not exceeding
$2,500. Every day any violation of this code or any such ordinance, rule or
regulation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. In any
prosecution based upon this section it shall be necessary to allege only the
first day with respect to which any forfeiture is assessable, and upon
conviction, the offender shall be assessed for that day and each day subsequent
thereto with respect to which it is proven and found that the person did commit
the violation.
('79 Code, § 1-10)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 30.01 COMPOSITION OF COMMON COUNCIL.
   The city shall be governed by I.C. 36-4-6-4 governing the makeup and method
of selection of members of the Common Council.
('79 Code, § 2-19) (Ord. 870, passed 10-13-81; Am. Ord. 36-1990, passed 12-24-
90)
Statutory reference:
   Common Council generally, see I.C. 36-4-6-1 et seq. 
   Authority, see I.C. 36-4-6-5
§ 30.02 COUNCILMANIC DISTRICTS.
   By reason of the provisions of I.C. 36-4-6-4, the territory of the city is
divided into five districts for the selection of members of the Common Council;
and the Common Council shall consist of seven members, one of whom shall be
elected from each of the districts hereafter described, and two shall be
elected at large by the voters of the city. The Council districts shall consist
as follows:
   (A)   District 1. District 1 shall consist of the territory incorporated in
Rochester Township Precinct Number 1 as that territory is described in the maps
and descriptions prepared by the County Election Board and on file in the
Office of the Clerk of the Fulton Circuit Court.
   (B)   District 2. District 2 shall consist of the territory incorporated in
Rochester Township Precinct Number 2 as that territory is described in the maps
and descriptions prepared by the County Election Board and on file in the
Office of the Clerk of the Fulton Circuit Court. In addition to the territory
incorporated in Precinct 2, District 2 shall include the territory annexed by
the city in Ordinance 19-1990, which additional territory is described in that
ordinance, and which additional territory is presently a part of Rochester
Township Precinct Number 6.
   (C)   District 3. District 3 shall consist of the territory incorporated in
Rochester Township Precinct Number 3 as that territory is described in the maps
and descriptions prepared by the County Election Board and on file in the
Office of the Clerk of the Fulton Circuit Court.
   (D)   District 4. District 4 shall consist of the territory incorporated in
Rochester Township Precinct Number 4 as that territory is described in the maps
and descriptions prepared by the County Election Board and on file in the
Office of the Clerk of the Fulton Circuit Court.
   (E)   District 5. District 5 shall consist of territory incorporated in
Rochester Township Precinct Number 5 as that territory is described in the maps
and descriptions prepared by the County Election Board and on file in the
Office of the Clerk of the Fulton Circuit Court.
('79 Code, § 2-124) (Ord. 903, passed 6-8-82; Am. Ord. 36-1990, passed 12-24-
90)
Statutory reference:
   Councilmanic districts generally, see I.C. 36-4-6-3 through 36-4-6-5
MEETINGS
§ 30.10 REGULAR MEETINGS.
   The regular and stated meetings of the Common Council shall be held in the
Council chamber at 6:00 p.m. on the fourth Tuesday evening of every month;
provided, however, the first regular meeting of any newly elected Council shall
be held on the first Monday in January after the election of officers at 6:00
p.m.
(‘79 Code, § 2-20) (Am. Ord. 08-2012, passed 7-10-12)
Statutory reference:
   Similar requirements, see I.C. 36-4-6-7
§ 30.11 CONTINUOUS SESSIONS.
   Any regular Common Council meeting may be adjourned to a future day or hour,
and at that time it shall be lawful to transact any business which might have
been transacted at the regular meeting of which it is a continuation, and the
Council shall not be limited to completing particular items of business which
had actually been entered upon and left unfinished, at the regular meeting,
unless the order of adjournment of such regular meeting so limits the work of
the adjourned meeting.
('79 Code, § 2-21)
§ 30.12 CALLING SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   Special meetings of the Common Council may be called by the Mayor or in
accordance with the rules of Common Council.
('79 Code, § 2-22)
Statutory reference:
   Calling of special Council meetings, see I.C. 36-4-5-3
§ 30.13 QUORUM.
   A majority of all the members-elect of the Common Council shall constitute a
quorum.
('79 Code, § 2-23)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 36-4-6-10
§ 30.14 APPOINTMENT OF STANDING AND SPECIAL COMMITTEES.

standing and special committees of the Common Council as he deems necessary.

PROCEDURE; RULES OF ORDER
§ 30.25 ADOPTION OF ROBERT'S RULES.
   (A)   There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing the procedure
to be followed by the Common Council and committees thereof, that certain
publication known as Robert's Rules of Order Newly Revised.
   (B)   In the event of a conflict between Robert's Rules and the other
provisions of this subchapter, the other provisions of this subchapter shall
prevail.
('79 Code, § 2-32)
Statutory reference:
   Power of Council to prescribe rules, see I.C. 36-4-6-6
§ 30.26 ORDER OF BUSINESS.
   (A)   Unless suspended by a two-thirds vote of the members of the Common
Council the business of the Council shall be taken up in the following order:
      (1)   Minutes of last meeting.
      (2)   Communications.
      (3)   Petitions, remonstrances and memorials.
      (4)   Reports of committees.
      (5)   Reports of officers.
      (6)   Ordinances and resolutions.
      (7)   Unfinished business.
      (8)   New business.
      (9)   Review of the most recently generated claims docket at the last
meeting of each month.
      (10)    Adjournment.
   (B)   The Common Council shall cause a copy of the agenda to be posted at
the entrance to the meeting.
('79 Code, § 2-33) (Ord. 41-1997, passed 12-23-97)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 5-14-1.5-4
§ 30.27 DUTIES OF MAYOR AT MEETINGS.
   The Mayor shall preside and preserve order and decorum at all meetings of
the Common Council, and shall decide questions of order, according to the
Council's rules.
('79 Code, § 2-34)
Statutory reference:
   Similar requirement, see I.C. 36-4-6-8
§ 30.28 PRESIDING OFFICER PRO TEMPORE.
   At the first regular meeting of the Common Council and on the first Monday
of every succeeding January, the Common Council shall choose from its members a
President pro tempore. In the absence of the Mayor, the President pro tempore
shall preside over the meeting of the Common Council.
('79 Code, § 2-35)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 36-4-6-8
§ 30.29 VOTING BY MAYOR.
   The Mayor shall not have the right to vote in meetings of the Common
Council, except that in the event of a tie vote, he shall be able to vote.
('79 Code, § 2-36)
Statutory reference:
   Similar requirements, see I.C. 36-4-6-8
§ 30.30 RIGHT OF MAYOR TO SPEAK ON POINTS OF ORDER.
   The Mayor shall be entitled to speak on all points of order at meetings of
the Common Council in preference to Councilmembers.
('79 Code, § 2-37)
§ 30.31 APPEAL FROM RULING OF MAYOR.
   An appeal from the Mayor's decision on any point of order to the Common
Council may be had upon the request of any member of the Council.
('79 Code, § 2-38)
§ 30.32 READING OF ORDINANCES.
   (A)   Every ordinance introduced before the Common Council shall be read
three times before its passage, but no ordinance shall be read the third time
at the same meeting at which it is introduced, except by unanimous consent and
then only in case there are present and voting at least two-thirds of the
members-elect.
('79 Code, § 2-39)
   (B)   Procedure.
      (1)   When an ordinance is introduced to the Common Council, it shall be
read by title, and the Chair [i.e., the Mayor or the Presiding Officer pro
tempore] shall state "This is the first reading of the ordinance; if there be
no objection it will go on to the second reading." If no objection be made or a
motion to reject fails, then the ordinance shall go to its second reading
without a question.
      (2)   The second reading of an ordinance shall be in full, except by
unanimous consent, and then only in case there are present and voting at least
two-thirds of the members-elect, the second reading may be by title only. Chair
shall state "This is the second reading of the ordinance."
      (3)   The third reading of an ordinance shall be by title. A motion for
passage must be made and seconded for a vote to be taken.
('79 Code, § 2-40) (Am. Ord. 19-2002, passed 9-10-02)
Statutory reference:
   Similar requirement, see I.C. 36-4-6-13
§ 30.33 MAJORITY VOTE REQUIRED TO PASS ORDINANCE.
   (A)   It shall require a majority vote of all the members-elect of the
Common Council to pass an ordinance.
   (B)   In the event that an ordinance is considered on the same day or at the
same meeting at which it is introduced, a two-thirds vote of all the elected
members is required to pass an ordinance.
('79 Code, § 2-41)
Statutory reference:
   Similar requirement, see I.C. 36-4-6-12 and 36-4-6-13
§ 30.34 APPROVAL AND VETO OF ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS BY MAYOR; OVERRIDING
VETO.
   Every ordinance, resolution or order of the Common Council shall,
immediately upon its passage, enrollment, attestation and signature by the
Clerk-Treasurer be presented by the Clerk-Treasurer to the Mayor and a record
of the time of such presentation made by the Clerk-Treasurer, and if the Mayor
approves it, he shall enter his approval thereon and sign the same and file it,
so signed in the office of the Clerk-Treasurer; if the Mayor does not approve
it, he shall return it to the Clerk-Treasurer with his objections in writing
within ten days after receiving it, and the Clerk-Treasurer shall then present
it to the Common Council at its next regular meeting. If the Mayor should fail
to discharge his duty by approving or disapproving such ordinance, resolution
or order within ten days, such failure shall be deemed a disapproval. In all
cases of disapproval by the Mayor such ordinance, resolution or order shall not
become a law, unless at the next Council meeting after the time named for the
Mayor's action, the Common Council again passes it by a two-thirds vote of all
the members-elect.
('79 Code, § 2-42)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 36-4-6-16
VIRTUAL MEETING POLICY
§ 30.40 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purposes of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MEMBERS. Members of the Rochester Common Council.
   VIRTUAL MEETING. A meeting in which one or more Council members meet by any
means of electronic communication, so long as (a) at least a quorum of the
members participate, (b) members can simultaneously communicate with each
other, and (c) the public is able to attend and observe the meeting (except for
executive session meetings). It includes meetings with a mix of electronic and
in-person attendance by members, but may include 100% electronic communication.
The minutes or memoranda for a virtual meeting must identify which members
attended and by which method, which were absent, and the means of electronic
communication used by members and the public. All votes taken in such a meeting
must be by roll call vote.
(Res. 04-2022, passed 4-26-22)
§ 30.41 DECLARED EMERGENCY MEETINGS.
   Whenever a disaster has been declared by either: the Indiana Governor
declaring a disaster emergency under I.C. 10-14-3-12; or the executive of the
city declaring a local disaster emergency under I.C. 10-14-3-29; the members of
the Council may meet in a virtual meeting.
(Res. 04-2022, passed 4-26-22)
§ 30.42 NON-EMERGENCY MEETINGS.
   This section shall apply whenever §
30.41 is not applicable.
   (A)   A member may attend a Council meeting using a virtual meeting, subject
to the conditions of this section. If doing so, a member is present for
purposes of establishing a quorum, and may participate in any final action so
long as the member can be seen and heard by other members and public attendees.
   (B)   A member should notify the President or Clerk-Treasurer at least 48
hours in advance of the meeting, if possible.
   (C)   At least 50% of the members must be physically present at the meeting.
This means no more than one member may participate virtually at any single
meeting.
   (D)   A member may not attend more than 50% of the meetings using a virtual
meeting format, or attend two consecutive meetings virtually, unless use of the
virtual meeting format is due to military service, illness or other medical
condition, death of a relative, or an emergency involving actual or threatened
injury to persons or property.
   (E)   A member may not participate in a meeting virtually if the Council is
attempting to take final action: to adopt a budget, make a reduction in
personnel; initiate a referendum; establish or increase a fee; establish or
increase a penalty; use the city’s eminent domain authority; or establish,
raise or renew a tax.
(Res. 04-2022, passed 4-26-22)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 31.01 OATH OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES.
   Every city officer before entering upon the duties of his office shall take
and subscribe an oath, to be indorsed on his certificate of election, and every
appointive office shall likewise take such oath, to be indorsed on his
certificate of appointment, before the Clerk-Treasurer, or some other officer
authorized to administer oaths, that he will support the Constitution of the
United States and the constitution of the state, and that he will faithfully
discharge all his official duties. The oath shall be filed with the Clerk-
Treasurer.
('79 Code, § 2-3)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 5-4-1-1 and 5-4-1-8
§ 31.02 BOND OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES.
   Except as otherwise provided by law, every city officer, except the Mayor
and the members of the Common Council, shall execute a bond to the approval of
the Mayor, payable to the city, in such penal sum as the Common Council may
provide by ordinance conditioned for the faithful performance of the duties of
his office and for the payment to the proper person of moneys received by him
as such officer.
('79 Code, § 2-4)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 5-4-1-5.1 and 5-4-1-8
§ 31.03 VACANCY IN OFFICES FOR FAILURE TO FILE OATH AND/OR BOND.
   Any city officer or employee who shall not file the oath and/or bond
required of him by law with the proper office within ten days after the
beginning of the term for which he shall have been elected or appointed, shall
be deemed to have refused to serve and the office shall be deemed to be vacant.
('79 Code, § 2-5)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 5-4-1-1.2
§ 31.04 FILLING VACANCY IN ELECTIVE OFFICE.
   Any vacancy which occurs in any elective city office shall be filled in the
manner provided by law.
('79 Code, § 2-6)
Statutory reference:
   Filling of vacancies in elective offices, see I.C. 3-13-8-1 et seq.
§ 31.05 DUTY OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES TO TURN OVER EFFECTS OF OFFICE.
   Upon the termination of his employment or service with the city, every city
officer and employee shall surrender to the city the effects of his office.
('79 Code, § 2-7)

§ 31.47 POWERS RELATIVE TO THE INTERNAL REVENUE SERVICE.
   (A)   The following express powers with respect to the Internal Revenue
Service are delegated to the Clerk-Treasurer:
      (1)   To give and receive information;
      (2)   To discuss any inquiries presented;
      (3)   To disagree with any and all proposed additions to tax;
      (4)   To appoint others to discuss specific issues with the IRS
personnel; and
      (5)   Represent the entity at all levels of IRS appeals, with direction
from the City Attorney and/or a certified public accountant.
   (B)   The Common Council reserves the following express powers with respect
to the Internal Revenue Service:
      (1)   To agree to and legally bind the entity to any and all proposed
additions to tax (settlements,etc.); and
      (2)   To sign documents to extend the statute of limitations.
(Res. 25-2005, passed 12-13-05)

section. The City Clerk is the clerk of the Board.

of the city at each bi-weekly meeting.

DEPARTMENT OF DEVELOPMENT
§ 32.15 CREATION.
   There is created a Department of Development under the control of a
commission to be known as “Rochester Development Commission.”
('79 Code, § 2-161)
§ 32.16 COMPOSITION OF COMMISSION.
   (A)   The Rochester Development Commission shall have five members to be
appointed in the manner provided under I.C. 36-7-12-5.
   (B)   No person shall be appointed as a Commissioner, who is not either a
resident of the city, employed in the city, or owner of a business in the city.
If any Commissioner shall cease to qualify in one of the above categories, his
appointment on the Board shall thereby terminate and his office shall become
vacant.
('79 Code, § 2-162) (Ord. 611, passed 2-25-75; Am. Ord. 833, passed 12-9-80)
PLAN COMMISSION
§ 32.25 ESTABLISHMENT OF COMMISSION.
   The Rochester City Plan Commission is hereby established.
('79 Code, § 2-136)
§ 32.26 COMPOSITION.
   The Plan Commission shall be composed of seven members.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93; Am. Ord. 18-1999, passed 8-24-99)
Statutory references:
   Membership of Commission, see I.C. 36-7-4-207
   Additional members to Commission, see I.C. 36-7-4-214
§ 32.27 MEMBERSHIP OF COMMISSION.
   The Plan Commission shall consist of the following members:
   (A)   The municipal legislative body shall appoint three persons, who must
be elected or appointed municipal officials or employees in the municipal
government, as members.
   (B)   The municipal executive shall appoint four citizen members, of whom no
more than two may be of the same political party.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93; Am. Ord. 18-1999, passed 8-24-99)
Statutory references:
   Membership of Commission, see I.C. 36-7-4-207
   Additional members to Commission, see I.C. 36-7-4-214
§ 32.28 QUALIFICATIONS OF CITIZEN MEMBERS.
   Each citizen member shall be appointed because of the member's knowledge and
experience in community affairs, the members awareness of the social, economic,
agricultural, and industrial problems of the area, and the member's interest in
the development and integration of the area. A citizen member may not hold
other elective or appointive office in municipal, county, or state government.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Qualifications of citizen members, see I.C. 36-7-4-216
§ 32.29 TERMS OF CITIZEN MEMBERS; REMOVAL.
   When an initial term of office of a citizen member expires, each new
appointment of a citizen member shall be for a term of four years. A member
serves until his successor is appointed and qualified. A member is eligible for
re-appointment. The appointing authority may remove a member from the Plan
Commission for cause. The appointing authority must mail notice of the removal,
along with written reasons for the removal, to the member at his residence
address. A member who is removed may, within 30 days after receiving notice of
the removal, appeal the removal to the Circuit or Superior Court of Fulton
County.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Appointments, terms and removal of members, see I.C. 36-7-4-218
§ 32.30 VACANCIES AMONG MEMBERS.
   If a vacancy on the Plan Commission occurs by resignation or otherwise, the
appointing authority shall appoint a member for the unexpired term of the
vacating member.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Vacancies, see I.C. 36-7-4-220
§ 32.31 CERTIFICATION OF MEMBERS.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall certify the appointment of the member appointed to
the Plan Commission by the Common Council. The Secretary of the Park Board
shall certify the member appointed to the Plan Commission by the Park Board.
The Secretary of the Board of Commissioners of Fulton County shall certify the
appointment by the members to the Plan Commission made by that body. The Mayor
shall certify his or her appointments to the membership of the Plan Commission.
The certificates shall be sent to and made part of the records of the Plan
Commission.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Certification of members, see I.C. 36-7-4-212
§ 32.32 QUORUM; MAJORITY REQUIRED FOR OFFICIAL ACTION.
   A majority of members of the Plan Commission shall constitute a quorum. No
action of the Commission is official, however, unless authorized by a majority
of the Commission at a regular or properly called special meeting.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory references:
   Quorum, see I.C. 36-7-4-301
   Official actions, see I.C. 36-7-4-302
§ 32.33 OFFICES AND PROPERTY OF COMMISSION.
   The city shall provide suitable offices for the holding of Plan Commission
meetings and for preserving the plans, maps, accounts, and other documents of
the Commission.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Offices and availability of records, see I.C. 36-7-4-305
§ 32.34 REGULAR MEETINGS.
   The Plan Commission shall fix the time for holding regular meetings each
month, or as necessary. The Commission shall keep minutes of its meetings. The
minutes of Commission meetings and all records shall be filed in the office of
the Commission and are public records.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Regular meetings and minutes, see I.C. 36-7-4-306
§ 32.35 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   Special meetings of the Plan Commission may be called by the President or by
two members of the Commission upon written request to the Secretary. The
Secretary shall send to all members, at least three days before the special
meeting, a written notice fixing the time and place of the meeting. A written
notice of a special meeting is not required if the date, time, and place of the
special meeting was fixed at a regular meeting at which all members of the
Commission were present.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Special meetings, see I.C. 36-7-4-307
§ 32.36 PRESIDENT AND VICE-PRESIDENT.
   At its first regular meeting in each year the Plan Commission shall elect
from its members a President and Vice-President. The Vice-President shall have
authority to act as President of the Commission during the absence or
disability of the President.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Election; Vice-President as acting President, see I.C. 36-7-4-303
§ 32.37 SECRETARY AND OTHER EMPLOYEES.
   The Plan Commission may appoint and prescribe the duties and fix the
compensation of the Secretary, and such employees as are necessary for the
discharge of the duties and responsibilities of the Commission. All such
compensation, however, shall be in conformity to and in compliance with
salaries and compensation theretofore fixed by the Common Council.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Appointment of Secretary, see I.C. 36-7-4-304
§ 32.38 DUTIES OF THE PLAN COMMISSION.
   The Plan Commission shall:
   (A)   Supervise, and make rules for, the administration of the affairs of
the Commission;
   (B)   Prescribe uniform rules pertaining to investigation and hearings;
   (C)   Keep a complete record of all proceedings;
   (D)   Record and file all bonds and contracts and assume responsibility for
the custody and preservation of all papers and documents of the Commission;
   (E)   Prepare, publish, and distribute reports, ordinances and other
material relating to its activities;
   (F)   Adopt a seal and certify to all official acts; and
   (G)   Exercise any and all powers and duties provided by state law and the
Common Council, even though not enumerated herein.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Duties of Plan Commission, see I.C. 36-7-4-401
§ 32.39 FEES.
   The Plan Commission shall establish a schedule of reasonable fees to defray
the administrative costs connected with processing and hearing administrative
appeals and petitions for re-zoning, special exceptions, special uses,
contingent uses, variances, issuing permits, and any other official action.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Establishment of fee schedule, see I.C. 36-7-4-411
§ 32.40 COMPREHENSIVE PLAN.
   The Plan Commission shall prepare a Comprehensive Plan to promote the public
health, safety, morals, convenience, order, and general welfare of the city to
enable efficient and economical development of the city. The Plan Commission
shall periodically review the Comprehensive Plan to ascertain the need, if any,
for amendment of the Plan.
(Ord. 3-1993, passed 1-26-93)
Statutory reference:
   Comprehensive Plan required, see I.C. 36-7-4-501
REDEVELOPMENT COMMISSION
§ 32.50 ESTABLISHMENT.
   The Common Council hereby establishes the Department of Redevelopment of the
city. The Department will be controlled by a board of five members known as the
Rochester Redevelopment Commission.
('79 Code, § 2-176) (Ord. 9-1990, passed 4-10-90)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see I.C. 36-7-14-1 through 36-7-14-40
§ 32.51 REDEVELOPMENT DISTRICT.
   Pursuant to I.C. 36-7-14-1 et seq. (i.e., the “state act”), all of the
territory within the corporate boundaries of the city will be a taxing district
to be known as the Redevelopment District of the city for the purpose of
levying and collecting special benefit taxes for redevelopment purposes as
provided in the state act. The Common Council finds and determines that all of
the taxable property within this special taxing district will be considered to
be benefitted by the redevelopment projects and economic development projects
carried out under the state act to the extent of the special taxes levied under
the state act.
('79 Code, § 2-177) (Ord. 9-1990, passed 4-10-90)
§ 32.52 COMMISSIONERS.
   Pursuant to I.C. 36-7-14-3 and I.C. 36-7-14-6.1, the Redevelopment
Commission shall consist of five commissioners, three of whom shall be
appointed by the Mayor and two of whom shall be appointed by the Common
Council, each of whom shall serve until January 1, 1992, or until their
successors are duly appointed and qualified.
('79 Code, § 2-178) (Ord. 9-1990, passed 4-10-90)
ARTS COMMISSION
§ 32.65 CREATION.
   There is created the Rochester Arts Commission.
('79 Code, § 2-191) (Ord. 6-1991, passed 4-23-91)
§ 32.66 COMPOSITION.
   The Rochester Arts Commission shall be composed of 16 to 21 members who
shall be appointed by the Mayor. Three members shall be appointed for a four-
year term, four members shall be appointed for a three-year term, four members
shall be appointed for a two-year term, and four members shall be appointed for
a one-year term. Other first-term members up to and including five such first-
term members may be appointed for terms of four years or less, at the
discretion of the Mayor. After the initial terms of the members, all subsequent
members shall be appointed for terms of four years.
('79 Code, § 2-192) (Ord. 6-1991, passed 4-23-91)
§ 32.67 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of the Rochester Arts Commission shall be to encourage, promote,
develop and program the still and performing arts for the benefit of the
community and its citizens.
('79 Code, § 2-193) (Ord. 6-1991, passed 4-23-91)
§ 32.68 AUTHORITY.
   The Rochester Arts Commission will have such lawful authority as may be
necessary to perform those acts and fulfill those duties as may be required to
fulfill the purposes of the Commission.
('79 Code, § 2-194) (Ord. 6-1991, passed 4-23-91)
DEPARTMENT OF STORMWATER MANAGEMENT
§ 32.75 AUTHORITY.
   I.C. 8-1.5-5 addressing the matter of stormwater management is hereby
adopted, making that chapter and any and all amendments thereto effective and
operative as to the city. The Board shall have the authority to exercise all
powers provided by I.C. 8-1.5-5-1 et seq.
(Ord. 22-2001, passed 11-27-01)
§ 32.76 CREATION.
   Pursuant to I.C. 8-1.5-5-1 et seq., a Department of Stormwater Management
shall be and is hereby created for the purpose of providing for the collection,
disposal and drainage of storm and surface water and relieving of sanitary
sewers of such water in the special taxing district which is also hereby
created pursuant to I.C. 8-1.5-5-1 et seq. The Department shall be administered
with the city municipal utilities. The Board of Directors shall be the Board of
Public Works and Safety that controls the city’s municipally owned utilities
pursuant to I.C. 8-2.5-5-4(g) and I.C. 8-1.5-3-3.
(Ord. 22-2001, passed 11-27-01; Am. Ord. 08-2011, passed 5-24-11)
§ 32.77 SPECIAL TAXING DISTRICT.
   The territory initially included in the special taxing district shall be and
is all of the territory now and hereafter included within the corporate limits
of the city.
(Ord. 22-2001, passed 11-27-01)
§ 32.78 FINANCES.
   The acquisition, construction, installation, operation and maintenance of
facilities and land for the stormwater system may be financed through the
proceeds of special taxing district bonds for the stormwater district; the
assumption of liability incurred to construct the stormwater system being
acquired; service rates; revenue bonds; or any other available funds. The
Board, after approval by the Common Council, may assess and collect user fees
from all of the property of the stormwater district for the operation and
maintenance of the stormwater system.
(Ord. 22-2001, passed 11-27-01; Am. Ord. 08-2011, passed 5-24-11)
FULTON COUNTY AREA PLAN COMMISSION
§ 32.90 ADOPTION.
   (A)   The City Council hereby adopts the Area Planning Law Establishing
Ordinance as contained in I.C. 36-7-4.
   (B)   The establishment of the planning department shall be fixed effective
the date of enactment of this section.
   (C)   The Fulton County Area Plan Commission is hereby established, whose
membership shall be appointed pursuant to I.C. 36-7-4.
(Ord. 17-2004, passed 11-23-04)
§ 32.91 COMMISSION MEMBERSHIP.
   Pursuant to I.C. 36-7-4-211, the legislative bodies of the Fulton County
Area Plan participants hereby change the representation of the Area Plan
Commission to consist of thirteen members as follows:
   (A)   One citizen member appointed by the County Commissioners, being the
executive body of thecounty:
      (1)   Who does not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who is a resident of the unincorporated area of the county.
   (B)   One citizen member appointed by the County Council, being the fiscal
body of the county:
      (1)   Who does not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who is a resident of the unincorporated area of the county.
   (C)   One member of the County Council, being the fiscal body of the county,
appointed from and by its membership.
   (D)   Two citizen members appointed by the Common Council of the city of
Rochester:
      (1)   Who do not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who are residents of the incorporated area of the city of
Rochester.
   (E)   One member of the Common Council of the city of Rochester, appointed
from and by its membership.
   (F)   Two citizen members appointed by the Town Council of the town of
Akron:
      (1)   Who do not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who are residents of the incorporated area of the Town of Akron.
   (G)   One citizen member appointed by the Town Council of the town of
Kewanna:
      (1)   Who does not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who is a resident of the incorporated area of the town of Kewanna.
   (H)   One citizen member appointed by the Town Council of the town of
Fulton:
      (1)   Who does not hold other elective or appointed office, except as
permitted in I.C. 36-7-4-902, in municipal, county, or state government.
      (2)   Who is a resident of the incorporated area of the town of Fulton.
   (I)   One member of the County Commissioners, being the executive body of
the county, appointed from and by its membership.
   (J)   The County Surveyor.
   (K)   The County Agricultural Extension Educator.
(Ord. 06-2005, passed 6-14-05)
CHAPTER 33: FIRE DEPARTMENT

Fire Chief and Assistant Fire Chief

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 33.01 ESTABLISHMENT.
   There is established a Fire Department.
('79 Code, § 5-19)
§ 33.02 MEMBERSHIP.
   The Fire Department shall consist of a Fire Chief, one Assistant Fire Chief,
and such additional members as may be required by the Common Council.
('79 Code, § 5-20)
Statutory reference:
   Power of Common Council to determine size of Fire Department, see I.C. 36-8-
2-3
§ 33.03 APPOINTMENT OF MEMBERS.
   All members of the Fire Department, including the Fire Chief and the
Assistant Fire Chief, shall be appointed by the Mayor.
('79 Code, § 5-21)
Statutory reference:
   Mayor to appoint firefighters, see I.C. 36-4-9-8
§ 33.04 CLASSIFICATION AND ADVANCEMENT OF MEMBERS.
   (A)   The Fire Department shall have the following membership
classifications:
      (1)   Probationary members.
      (2)   Second class members.
      (3)   First class members.
   (B)   Upon first being appointed, a firefighter shall serve at least 12
months in the probationary class before becoming eligible for promotion. In
addition the candidate must successfully complete the required schooling for a
second class or first class firefighter prior to promotion.
   (C)   Any advancement in classification or increase in compensation shall
become effective on January 1 or July 1, whichever comes first after the
firefighter becomes eligible for such advancements.
('79 Code, § 5-22)
Statutory reference:
   Probationary appointments, see I.C. 36-8-4-12
§ 33.05 SUSPENSION OR DISMISSAL OF MEMBERS.
   All firefighters, including the Fire Chief and the Assistant Fire Chief,
shall be suspended or dismissed from their positions in the manner provided by
state law.
('79 Code, § 5-27)
Statutory reference:
   Suspension or dismissal of firefighters, see I.C. 36-8-3-4
§ 33.06 PENSION FUND AND BOARD OF TRUSTEES ESTABLISHED.
   Pursuant to I.C. 36-8-7-3 there is established a 1937 Firefighter's Pension
Fund and a local Board of Trustees to manage, use, and disburse the fund for
the benefit of those firefighters, either active or retired, who were hired
prior to May 1, 1977 and are not otherwise members of the 1977 Police Officers'
and Firefighters' Pension and Disability Fund.
FIRE CHIEF AND ASSISTANT FIRE CHIEF
§ 33.15 POWERS OF FIRE CHIEF AND ASSISTANT FIRE CHIEF.
   The Fire Chief has exclusive control of the fire department subject to the
rules and orders of the Board of Public Works and Safety. However, in times of
emergency, the Fire Chief is, for the time being, subordinate to the Mayor and
shall obey his orders and directions.”
§ 33.16 ARREST POWERS.
   Both the Fire Chief and the Assistant Fire Chief shall, while in attendance
at any fire within the city limits have the power to arrest any person who is
interfering in any way with the functions of the Fire Department or its
equipment.
('79 Code, § 5-25)
§ 33.17 DUTIES.
   In addition to all other duties provided by law, the Fire Chief and the
Assistant Fire Chief during their respective hours of duty shall:
   (A)   Be in constant attendance upon their respective duties.
   (B)   Keep the fire station and all firefighting apparatus clean and in a
good condition at all times.
   (C)   Promptly answer all fire alarms occurring within the city limits.
   (D)   Promptly answer all fire alarms occurring outside of the city limits
when directed to do so by the Mayor.
   (E)   Be responsible for the care, custody and control of all firefighting
equipment.
('79 Code, § 5-26)
CHAPTER 34: POLICE DEPARTMENT
Section
General Provisions
   
34.01   Establishment
   
34.02   Composition of Department
   
34.03   Appointment of Chief of Police and other members

34.06   Duties performed under supervision of Mayor
   
34.07   Special police

34.10   Power of Chief to direct police

34.25   Records concerning police
   
34.26   Records concerning criminals

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 34.01 ESTABLISHMENT.
   There is established a Police Department.
('79 Code, § 12-1)
Statutory reference:
   Power of city to establish Police Department, see I.C. 36-8-2-2
§ 34.02 COMPOSITION OF DEPARTMENT.
   The Police Department shall consist of a Chief of Police and as many
additional officers and persons as required by law.
('79 Code, § 12-2)
§ 34.03 APPOINTMENT OF CHIEF OF POLICE AND OTHER MEMBERS.
   The Chief of Police and any other employee of the police department who
holds an upper level policy making position shall be appointed by the Mayor.
All other members and employees of the police department are appointed by the
Board of Public Works and Safety.
('79 Code, § 12-3)
Statutory references:
   Appointment of police officers, see I.C. 36-8-3-3
   Appointment of Police Chief, see I.C. 36-4-9-8
§ 34.04 CLASSIFICATION OF POLICE OFFICERS.
   The classifications of probationary, second class and first class are
established in the Police Department.
('79 Code, § 12-4)
§ 34.05 ADVANCEMENT AND COMPENSATION.
   (A)   Upon first being appointed, a police officer with no experience must
serve at least 12 months in the probationary class before becoming eligible for
promotion to police officer.
   (B)   With prior experience before appointment to the Police Department, a
police officer starting the probationary class may receive a pay raise prior to
promotion to first class officer, at the discretion of the Board of Public
Works.
('79 Code, § 12-5) (Ord.25-1997, passed 8-26-97)
§ 34.06 DUTIES PERFORMED UNDER SUPERVISION OF MAYOR.
   The Chief of Police has exclusive control of the police department subject
to the rules and orders of the Board of Public Works and Safety. However, in
times of emergency, the Chief of Police is, for the time being, subordinate to
the Mayor and shall obey the Mayor’s orders and directions, notwithstanding any
law or rule to the contrary.
(I.C. 36-8-3-3)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 36-8-3-3
§ 34.07 SPECIAL POLICE.
   (A)   Whenever the public safety requires an increase of the police force,
in the judgment of the Board of Public Works and Safety or, in the case of
emergency, the Mayor shall appoint as many suitable persons as may be necessary
to act as special police, who shall be sworn in and furnished with police
equipment. They shall be under the control of the Chief of Police when they are
on duty.
   (B)   The city may grant authority to the Rochester Community School
Corporation to provide security/school resource officer(s) under the authority
of the special police.
      (1)   The officer(s) are to be provided at the expense and liability of
the Rochester Community School Corporation.
      (2)   The officer(s) are to provide primary police service to the
Rochester Community School Corporation and its grounds at the direction of the
School Superintendent and School Board.
('79 Code, § 12-7) (Am. Ord. 22-2000, passed 10-24-00)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 36-8-3-3
§ 34.08 UNIFORMS.
   While on duty all members of the Police Department shall wear the standard-
type police uniform. ('79 Code, § 12-8)
§ 34.09 DISPLAY OF POLICE INSIGNIA.
   The Chief of Police and every police officer, while on duty, shall wear in
some conspicuous place on the breast a star with the word “police” written or
engraved thereon. It shall be exhibited whenever required.
('79 Code, § 12-9)
§ 34.10 POWER OF CHIEF TO DIRECT POLICE.
   The Chief of Police shall direct any or all members of the police force to
any place where their services are deemed necessary.
('79 Code, § 12-10)
§ 34.11 DUTIES OF POLICE OFFICERS.
   Each police officer shall be a conservator of public peace and shall enforce
all laws.
('79 Code, § 12-11)
Statutory reference:
   Powers of police, see I.C. 36-8-3-6
§ 34.12 REPORTS TO CHIEF OF POLICE.
   It shall be the duty of each police officer to report to the Chief of Police
or his designated representative on his scheduled period of duty.
('79 Code, § 12-12)
§ 34.13 SUSPENDING OR DISCHARGING MEMBERS.
   The members of the Police Department may not be suspended or discharged
without a hearing by the Board of Public Works and Safety as provided by law.
('79 Code, § 12-17)
Statutory reference:
   Suspension or discharge of police officers, see I.C. 36-8-3-4
§ 34.14 FEE FOR FURNISHING ACCIDENT REPORTS.
   (A)   Directed. The Police Department is directed to charge $12 for every
accident report it furnishes to anyone, other than another law enforcement
agency.
   (B)   Monthly Deposit Required. The Police Department is directed to deposit
said fees with the Clerk-Treasurer on a monthly basis, which the Clerk-
Treasurer is to deposit into the local law enforcement continuing education
fund.
('79 Code, § 12-18) (Ord. 873, passed 10-27-81; Am. Ord. 07-2002, passed 4-9-
02; Am. Ord. 11-2007, passed 7-24-07)
RECORDS
§ 34.25 RECORDS CONCERNING POLICE OFFICERS.
   The Chief of Police shall keep in his office a book in which he shall enter
the names and addresses of every police officer together with the date of their
appointment.
('79 Code, § 12-13)
§ 34.26 RECORDS CONCERNING CRIMINALS
   The Chief of Police shall keep in his office a book in which he shall enter
the name and alias of every person against whom a criminal charge is preferred,
and the disposition made thereof.
('79 Code, § 12-14)
§ 34.27 PROPERTY RECORDS.
   The Chief of Police shall keep in his office a book in which shall be
entered a detailed account of all property which may have come into his
possession, or in the possession of the Police Department, in whose possession
it was found, and by whom, and whether the property was stolen or otherwise,
and also how such property was disposed of. ('79 Code, § 12-15)
§ 34.28 COPIES OF COMMUNICATIONS.
   The Chief of Police shall keep a copy of all official communications issued
from his office.
('79 Code, § 12-16)
CHAPTER 35: FINANCE AND REVENUE; FUNDS
Section
Funds

FUNDS
FUNDS
§ 35.01 GENERAL IMPROVEMENT FUND.
   (A)   There is established a fund to be known as the General Improvement
Fund.
   (B)   This fund shall be used as a fund to pay for the construction, repair
or improvement of streets, alleys, sidewalks, curbs, gutters and sewers.
   (C)   This fund shall consist of funds realized from the collection of all
special assessments for benefit to property from the construction, repair or
improvement of streets, alleys, sidewalks, curbs, gutters and sewers, together
with any appropriation made from the General Fund of the city, or from taxes
levied by the Common Council for such purposes; provided, however, that no
money received from the collection of special assessments assessed for benefits
to property under provisions of the Barrett Law and special assessments as are
now or may hereafter be provided by law shall be deposited in this fund, except
as otherwise provided by state law.
   (D)   The aggregate sum which will be appropriated or levied shall not
exceed the equivalent of $.50 on each $100 net taxable valuation of the real
and personal property in the city.
('79 Code, § 2-1)
Statutory reference:
   General Improvement Fund, see I.C. 36-9-17-1 et seq.
§ 35.02 CUMULATIVE CAPITAL IMPROVEMENT FUND.
   (A)   There is established a special fund to be known as the Cumulative
Capital Improvement Fund into which the cigarette taxes allotted to the city by
state law shall be deposited. This fund shall be a cumulative fund and all of
the monies deposited into the fund shall be appropriated and used solely for
capital improvements, and none of such monies shall revert to the General Fund
of the city or be used for any purposes other than capital improvements.
   (B)   For the purpose of this section, the following definition shall apply.
      CAPITAL IMPROVEMENTS. The construction or improvement of any property
owned by the city, including but not limited to streets, thoroughfares and
sewers and the retirement of the city's general obligation bonds, and the
proceeds used for the purpose of constructing capital improvements; it shall
not include salaries of any public officials or employees except those which
are directly chargeable to a capital improvement.
('79 Code, § 2-2) (Ord. 311, passed 5-11-65)
Statutory reference:
   Cumulative Capital Improvement Fund required, see I.C. 6-7-1-31.1
   Allocation of monies by state to city, see I.C. 6-7-1-30.1
§ 35.03 PARKS AND RECREATION CAPITAL FUND.
   (A)   A special non-reverting capital fund, which has been established in
addition to the general park fund, which is created for the purpose of
acquiring land or making specific capital improvements from which expenditures
may be made upon appropriation by the Council. The non-reverting park capital
improvement fund shall be funded in the following manner:
      (1)   By monies and fees procured from the sale and/or disposition of
land, property, facilities, and equipment that is no longer of use to the
Board.
      (2)   From all profit of the Round Barn Golf Course at Mill Creek, 10% of
the amount in excess of the anticipated gross revenues of the Round Barn Golf
Course at Mill Creek, as set forth in the annual budget calculations for any
given year.
      (3)   All monies acquired from the rental of picnic shelters and picnic
sites.
      (4)   Monies received from donations or grants received from the general
public or governmental agencies which are designated for use in the
construction of a particular capital improvement, as well as donations and
grants which are not designated for any particular purpose.
      (5)   Monies from the general park fund which the Council may, from time
to time, appropriate for such purpose.
      (6)   Seventy percent of the income from the rental of golf carts at the
Round Barn Golf Course at Mill Creek.
   (B)   Disbursements shall be made from the special non-reverting park
capital improvement fund on approved claims allowed and signed by the president
and the secretary of the Board following appropriation by the Council.
(Ord. 37-1994, passed 11-22-94; Am. Ord. 05-1999, passed 3-9-99; Am. Ord. 11-
2011, passed 9-27-11; Am. Ord. 04-2021, passed 3-23-21)
§ 35.04 PARKS AND RECREATION OPERATING FUND.
   (A)   A special non-reverting park operating fund, in addition to the
general park fund, is also hereby established for the purpose of the operation
and maintenance of parks and for recreation programs and activities.
Expenditures from the special non-reverting park operating fund shall be made
by appropriation of the Board and disbursed only on approved claims allowed and
signed by the president and secretary of the Board. The special non-reverting
park operating fund shall be funded in the following manner:
      (1)   Monies and fees procured from summer park and recreation programs
and activities, other than those collected from the operation of the swimming
pool.
      (2)   Monies and fees procured from concessions, either by direct sales,
rentals or leases, as well as money derived from the rental of any park
property, either real or personal, other than picnic shelters and sites.
      (3)   Donations or grants from the general public or other governmental
agencies which are specifically designated for the purpose of operating a park
recreation program or activity.
      (4)   Monies from the general park fund which the Council may, from time
to time, appropriate for such purpose.
      (5)   Thirty percent of the income from the golf cart rental of the Round
Barn Golf Course at Mill Creek for the maintenance of the carts.
   (B)   The Board may, from time to time, direct the transfer of funds from
the special non-reverting park operating fund to the non-reverting park capital
improvement fund or from the non-reverting park capital improvement fund to the
non-reverting park operating fund.
(Ord. 37-1994, passed 11-22-94; Am. Ord. 11-2011, passed 9-27-11)
§ 35.05 COMMUNITY HOST FEE FUND.
   (A)   A non-reverting Community Host Fee Fund is hereby established.
   (B)   The Clerk/Treasurer shall deposit all funds received pursuant to any
host fee agreement into this fund.
   (C)   This cumulative fund shall remain in effect until the county line
landfill is closed.
(Ord. 11-1999, passed 4-27-99)
§ 35.06 POLICE CRIME-PREVENTION FUND.
   The Common Council hereby establishes a non-reverting fund for the receipt
of donations to thePolice Crime-Prevention Fund, accruing all earnings upon
investment to the fund, in compliance withrules and regulations of the state
Board of Tax Commissioners, the fund to be a non-reverting cumulative fund to
be used for projects such as public relations for the Police Department and
advertising, including but not limited to stickers, hats, children’s
fingerprint kits, and the like.
(Ord. 03-2000, passed 2-22-00; Am. Ord. 11-2004, passed 7-13-04)
§ 35.07 RAINY DAY FUND.
   (A)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall establish a Rainy Day Fund to receive
transfers of unused and unencumbered funds raised by a general or special tax
levy on taxable property within the city whenever the purpose of such levy has
been fulfilled and an unused and unencumbered balance remains.
   (B)   The funds on deposit in the Rainy Day Fund may be used for the
operation of the city and its various departments when the city does not have
sufficient levies or funds to pay such costs, including, but not limited to,
purchase of equipment, payment of operating expenses of any department or
office of the civil city, or for any other purpose for which property taxes may
be imposed.
   (C)   The Common Council shall determine the amount, if any, of any unused
and unencumbered prior year funds available to be transferred to the Rainy Day
Fund, which transfer may not exceed more than 10% of the city’s total budget
for said fiscal year.
   (D)   The Common Council may authorize the expenditure of funds from the
Rainy Day Fund by appropriations made in the same manner as other funds are
appropriated that receive tax monies, upon making a finding that the proposed
use of the funds is consistent with the intent of the fund.
(Ord. 26-2001, passed 1-8-02)
§ 35.08 RIVERBOAT WAGERING TAX REVENUE SHARING FUND.
   The city being desirous of creating a fund for the share of riverboat
wagering tax revenue sharing hereby establishes by resolution a Riverboat
Wagering Tax Revenue Sharing Fund to receipt the city’s distribution to that
fund for the purposes allowed in I.C. 4-33-13-5(f).
(Res. 20-2003, passed 8-26-03)
§ 35.09 CUMULATIVE CAPITAL DEVELOPMENT FUND.
   (A)   The Common Council hereby establishes a Cumulative Capital Development
Fund for all uses as set out in I.C. 36-9-15.5. This Board will adhere to the
provisions of I.C. 36-9-15.5. The proposed fund will not exceed $.05 on each
$100 of assessed valuation. The tax rate will be levied beginning with taxes
for 2023 payable 2024.
   (B)   The Common Council hereby re-establishes the Cumulative Capital
Development Fund beginning in the year 2014. Notwithstanding division (A),
funds accumulated in the Cumulative Capital Development Fund may be spent for
purposes other than those stated therein, if the purpose is to protect the
public health, welfare or safety in an emergency situation that demands
immediate action. Money may be spent under the authority of this section only
after the Mayor issues a declaration that the public health, welfare or safety
is in immediate danger that requires the expenditure of money in the fund. This
fund takes effect upon approval of the Department of Local Government Finance.
(Ord. 07-2005, passed 7-26-05; Am. Ord. 07-2013, passed 6-7-13; Am. Res. 02-
2023, passed 3-28-23)
