GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 52.001 OPERATION OF MUNICIPAL WATER WORKS.
   The municipal waterworks of the city shall be operated in accordance with
the provisions of I.C. 8-1.5-4-1 through 8-1.5-4-9, and subject to all the
terms, conditions, and regulations contained therein, as said sections shall be
amended by any subsequent amendment.
('79 Code, § 17-16) (Ord. 931, passed 12-14-82)
§ 52.002 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CONSUMER. The person who has an interest, either legal or equitable, sole,
or partial, either as tenant or owner, in any property which is, or is about to
be supplied with water service by the city.
('79 Code, § 17-77)
§ 52.003 LOANING CURB STOP KEY.
   Neither the Water Department nor any officer or employee thereof, nor any
plumber shall give or loan a curb stop key to any person.
('79 Code, § 17-29)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.004 SHUTTING OFF WATER; NOTICE.
   The city reserves the right at any time, without notice, to shut off the
water in the street mains for repairs, extensions, or for any other purposes.
All persons having any apparatus connected to the water system dependent on the
water pressure are cautioned against danger of collapse when the supply is cut
off. When circumstances permit, the consumer will be advised of a shut-off by
public notice or otherwise, but in no case shall the city, the Board of
Directors, the Superintendent of the Waterworks or any other city employee be
held for damages resulting from failure from any cause to supply water to any
consumer.
('79 Code, § 17-30) (Ord. 931, passed 12-14-82)
§ 52.005 SUPERINTENDENT; APPOINTMENT AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The Board of Directors shall annually at the first meeting in the
month of January of each year appoint a Superintendent of the Waterworks, whose
term of office shall be for one year and who shall have immediate control under
the direction of the Directors of the operation of the waterworks.
   (B)   The Superintendent shall be responsible to the Directors for the
proper operation of the waterworks and he shall have the power and/or duty to:
      (1)   See that the rules and regulations adopted by the Directors or
enacted by ordinance are properly executed; he shall also see that the
conditions of all contracts are faithfully complied with and shall superintend
all repairs of the waterworks ordered by the Directors and shall cause the same
to be done in accordance with the orders and directions of the Directors.
      (2)   Inspect all extensions and improvements of the waterworks that may
be hereafter authorized and cause the same to be done according to the contract
therefor made.
      (3)   Superintend and inspect all connections of service pipe with the
main and for extensions therefrom to the stop and box at the sidewalk including
stop-box, and all material used in tapping mains and in running the service
pipe used from the mains to the corporation stop at the sidewalk including the
stop-box shall be subject to his inspection and he shall cause the plumber and
his employees engaged in doing the work to strictly conform to all bylaws,
rules, regulations and ordinances relating thereto.
      (4)   Keep in repair all the fire hydrants, belonging to the waterworks
and flush all hydrants when necessary, keeping the working parts well oiled and
especially see that each and every fire hydrant is at all times ready for
immediate use.
      (5)   At the first meeting of the Directors of each month make a
financial and working report to the Directors, and not later than the first of
each month, report all consumers who are delinquent in the payment of their
water bills to the Directors; when the Directors shall order the water shut off
with respect to any delinquent user, the Superintendent shall immediately
discontinue the service, to be turned on again.
('79 Code, § 17-26) (Ord. 931, passed 12-14-82)
Statutory reference:
   Appointment of superintendent, see I.C. 8-1.5-3-4(a)(3)
§ 52.006 CASHIER; APPOINTMENT AND DUTIES.
   (A)   At the first meeting of the Board of Directors in the month of January
of each year, the Directors shall appoint a Cashier for the waterworks, fix the
compensation therefor and require the Cashier to furnish bond for the
satisfactory performance of the duties of the Cashier in the penal sum of not
less than $1,000 with surety to the approval of the Trustees.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of the Cashier to make all bills to consumers for
water used upon report of the Superintendent of meter readings and for any
other service that may be utilized other than through meters, receive all money
due to the waterworks from the consumers for service furnished, and daily
deposit with the Clerk-Treasurer all funds received by such cashier during any
day that collections are made by the cashier pursuant to this chapter.
('79 Code, § 17-27) (Ord. 931, passed 12-14-82)

§ 52.007 PAYMENT FOR LOST WATER.
   (A)   Definition. Person is meant to be developer, contractor, landowner,
agent, or anyone else that causes water losses.
   (B)   Lost water. It is hereby ordained that henceforth any person working
within the boundaries of the Rochester Water Works Department jurisdiction be
ordered to pay the Water Works Department of the city for lost water from a
broken water main caused by a person. Payment is to be at the rate of
“Rochester Lost Water Revenue Estimate” already established at the time the
water main is broken or from back-flushing or any other water loss created by
the person. (Refer to the Rochester Lost Water Revenue Estimate Chart on file
at the Water Department.)
(Ord. 06-2002, passed 5-14-02)
CONNECTIONS AND MAINTENANCE REGULATIONS
§ 52.015 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any premises, which is now
or may hereafter be supplied with water from any service line or attachment,
connection, or extensions thereto, to make any attachments thereto or
extensions of the service line or any attachment, connections, or extensions of
the service line without first having made an application therefor and
obtaining permission from the Superintendent of the Waterworks Department.
('79 Code, § 17-37)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.016 APPLICATION FOR SERVICE.
   Any person desiring a supply of water from a city water main shall apply in
writing and on the application form shall state that he will in all things
abide by the applicable provisions of this code and any other ordinance of the
city, and any rules and regulations of the waterworks system.
('79 Code, § 17-38)
§ 52.017 APPLICATION FORM; METER DEPOSITS.
   (A)   An application for water service shall be in the form prescribed by
the Waterworks Department.
   (B)   Whenever an application is made for the use of city water by any
person or organization, the Superintendent of the Department of Waterworks
shall require the person to make a meter deposit with the Clerk-Treasurer of
the city.
      (1)   For an application for water service to a single-family residence,
the meter deposit shall be $75.
      (2)   On an application for water service for a business or commercial
installation, the meter deposit shall be $125.
   (C)   In the event of the default by any consumer in the payment of his
water bill, the Waterworks Department shall have the right to charge the same
against the meter deposit when the unpaid bill shall equal or exceed the amount
of the meter deposit.
('79 Code, § 17-39) (Ord. 951, passed 7-26-83; Am. Ord. 32-1985, passed 10-22-
85; Am. Ord. 23-1989, passed 6-13-89; Am. Ord. 09-2006, passed 8-22-06; Am.
Ord. 10-2021, passed 8-24-21)

§ 52.018 TAPPING FEES.
   Tap charges shall be made from each customer prior to connection to the
water system as follows:
   (A)   All installations completed by the Water Department will be for one
inch taps only and the fee shall be $5,000. Except as stated in division (B)
below, no tapping fee shall be incurred when existing infrastructure designed
to serve multiple properties is dedicated to, and accepted by, the Water
Department, where no installation is completed by the Water Department.
   (B)   For installations larger than one inch, the customer is responsible
for all installation and applicable charges including any damages to the water
main, meter pit, and/or curb stop. In addition, all installations must be
inspected and approved by the Water Department prior to service being started.
Any taps larger than one-inch will also pay the fee listed in division (A) to
the Water Department.
(‘79 Code, § 17-40) (Ord. 686, passed 7-27-77; Am. Ord. 703, passed 2-14-78;
Am. Ord. 3-1991, passed 2-26-91; Am. Ord. 23-1995, passed 11-14-95; Am. Ord.
04-2013, passed 4-23-13; Am. Ord. 09-2017, passed 11-28-17; Am. Ord. 10-2021,
passed 8-24-21; Am. Ord. 02-2022, passed 8-23-22; Am. Ord. 07-2023, passed 12-

§ 52.019 INSTALLATION AND PIPE COSTS.
   (A)   Upon payment of all required fees and costs, the Clerk-Treasurer shall
issue the water service applicant a receipt and the receipt shall be presented
to the Superintendent of the Waterworks and the city will then cause the water
main to be tapped and service pipe of the size designated connected with the
main and laid to the tree line in front of the premises to be served with
water, provided there is a city water main in the street adjacent to the
premises.
   (B)   If there is no such water main, then the service pipe will be
designated an extended line and the applicant shall pay the regular tapping
fees, and in addition thereof, in the event the distance of the extended line
exceeds 20 feet, the following fees shall be charged:
 
Size of Service (inches) Cost per Foot
¾                       $ 1.25
1                        1.75
1½                      2.00
2                        2.25
 
   (C)   These fees and costs shall include the tapping, furnishing and laying
of a service pipe corporation stop, stop-box and curb stop.
('79 Code, § 17-41)
Cross-reference:
   
Rates and charges, see § 52.096
§ 52.020 TAPPING PERMIT; MANNER OF TAPPING; SPECIFICATIONS OF MATERIALS USED.
   (A)   Whenever it shall be necessary to tap the water main and lay water
service pipes and connections, and if fees have been paid in accordance with
the provisions of this chapter, the applicant shall present the receipt of the
Clerk-Treasurer to the Superintendent of the Waterworks Department who will
then issue to the holder of the receipt a permit to connect with service pipe
to the main. Upon issuance of the permit the city will cause laid water main to
be tapped and the service pipe of the size mentioned in the permit to be
connected with the main and laid to the tree line in front of the premises to
be served with water.
   (B)   All tapping and making connections with the street main and laying the
service pipes, corporation stops and stop boxes shall be done by the Water
Department, provided however, that in making the tap only registered plumbers,
hired by the Waterworks Department, shall be permitted to make the tap. When
the work of laying the service line and the tapping has been completed the
Superintendent shall make inspection and, if he approves, shall then order the
water turned on.
   (C)   All water mains shall be of cast-iron material; all service lines of
two inches or less shall be of copper material, and all service lines of more
than two inches shall be of cast-iron material. The material shall be of a
quality approved by the Superintendent of the Waterworks.
   (D)   All attachments for copper service pipes will be made by means of a
flared fitting, of the best material and workmanship, and for all attachments
to mains for supplies greater than 3/4 inch, the Board of Waterworks Trustees
reserves the right to designate the size and number of taps to be made, and the
size and kind of service pipe to be laid.
   (E)   The corporation cock shall be best quality of yellow brass, round way
ground stop, with “T” handles.
   (F)   All service pipes shall be laid not less than four and one-half feet
below the surface of the ground at all points. The stop boxes shall be of first
quality adjustable to height with the words “City Water” cast on the lid and
the boxes so set that the top of the box will be at a grade to be designated by
the Waterworks Department.
('79 Code, § 17-42) (Ord. 335, passed 8-10-65)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.021 AUTHORIZATION REQUIRED TO TAP OR MAKE CONNECTION.
   No person shall be permitted to tap or make any connections with the
distributing pipes of the waterworks unless duly authorized.
('79 Code, § 17-43)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.022 REGISTERED PLUMBER TO MAKE ATTACHMENTS WITH MAIN PIPES; PERMIT
REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to make any attachments to water service
connected with the main pipes of the waterworks, or make any addition or
alteration of any kind to tap, pipe, cock or other fixture connected with the
pipe supply to consumers from the waterworks unless he is a plumber registered
with the Clerk-Treasurer; provided however, that nothing in this section shall
authorize a plumber to make any attachments, alterations, additions or do any
other work in connection with or for the purpose of supplying water from the
waterworks without the required permit.
('79 Code, § 17-44)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.023 CONSUMERS TO MAINTAIN PIPES AND FIXTURES; REPAIR BREAKS; LIABILITY.
   (A) All water consumers shall keep their service pipes and fixtures from the
street mains in repair and in good working order at their own expense. It is
expressly stipulated that no claim shall be allowed by reason of damages to the
consumers' property as a result of the breaking of any service cock or service
pipe. In case of a break in any service pipe the owners of the property shall
repair the pipe immediately, and on failure to do so, after being notified, the
Waterworks Department will repair the pipe and the repairs shall be added to
the water bill of the consumer and shall be paid by the consumer and the
failure to do so shall subject the consumer to such penalty collection charges
as is provided in the case of a delinquent water bill, including the liability
of having the supply of water shut off.
   (B)   The water consumer shall be held liable for any damages to the public
generally, resulting from failure to immediately protect and repair a leak in
his water service.
('79 Code, § 17-45)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.024 CONSUMERS LIABLE FOR CITY SERVICE TO FROZEN PIPES; MULTIPLE CUSTOMERS
ON SAME LINE PROHIBITED.
   (A)   In case the city furnishes any service with respect to thawing any
frozen water pipes, either in the service pipe and connections or to pipes
located on a consumer's premises, the consumer shall pay the amount as may be
fixed by the Board of Waterworks Trustees, and the charge shall be added to the
regular water bill of the consumer, and the nonpayment thereof shall be subject
to the penalty collection charge and the liability of having the water
disconnected as is provided with respect to repairs made by the city.
   (B)   In the passage of this chapter it is expressly stipulated that not
more than one consumer can be supplied from one tap to the water main or one
service line.
('79 Code, § 17-46)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.025 WATERWORKS DEPARTMENT TURNING WATER OFF AND ON; CHARGE.
   The Waterworks Department shall make all water service turn-ons and turn-
offs. A service charge of $20 will be made to the property owner or water user
for each turn-on and each turn-off made by the Department Monday through
Friday, from 7:00 a.m. to 3:00 p.m. A service charge of $40 will be made for
turn-offs at all other times, and there will be no turn-ons outside normal
business hours.
(‘79 Code, § 17-47) (Ord. 335, passed 8-10-65; Am. Ord. 951, passed 7-26-83;
Am. Ord. 23-1989, passed 6-13-89; Am. Ord. 10-2021, passed 8-24-21)
Cross-reference:
   
Rates and charges, see §§ 52.095 et seq.
§ 52.026 REPAIR BY CITY; LIABILITY FOR DAMAGES FROM TURNING WATER ON OR OFF.
   The Waterworks Department will not make any repair work nor attempt to drain
any plumbing and shall not be responsible for any damage done to property due
to turning on or turning off the water; where pipes needing draining or which
are out of order the consumer shall assume full responsibility for draining or
repairs.
('79 Code, § 17-48) (Ord. 335, passed 8-10-65)
§ 52.027 VALVES TO BE INSTALLED WHERE PRIVATE WELLS USED IN CONJUNCTION WITH
CITY WATER.
   Whenever private well supplies are used to supply boilers or there are any
cross connections with the city's water mains, there must be installed check
valves and gate valves as approved by the State Board of Health to prevent any
private supply from backing up into the city's water mains.
('79 Code, § 17-49)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.028 CLOSING CORPORATION STOP AND TURNING WATER OFF.
   Any plumber who has made any connection with a water service pipe leading to
a water main, made any addition thereto, added or changed any fixture or done
any other work by which water is to be conveyed into any fixture or done any
other work by which water is to be used, or can be used, after turning and
leaving the water on sufficiently long to test the work, must close the
corporation stop at the tree line and leave the water turned off and
immediately make his return to the Superintendent of the Waterworks Department.
The failure to do so shall be grounds to revoke his registration.
('79 Code, § 17-50)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.029 ATTACHING PIPE TO STOPCOCK.
   Whenever any plumber has occasion to attach any pipe to a stopcock at the
tree line, either in new work or in case of repairs, he must see that the tee
on the stopcock is left in the center of the stop box and the stop box well
secured to prevent removal or displacement in filling around it or settling of
such filling.
('79 Code, § 17-51)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.030 INSPECTION AND APPROVAL BY SUPERINTENDENT.
   All plumbers working on a water connection shall allow the Superintendent of
the Waterworks to inspect any and all work so done by him or them before the
trenches are filled up and before the water is turned into the building so
plumbed and to this end he shall notify the Superintendent when the work is
completed and ready for inspection and no water shall be turned into the pipes
connecting the waterworks mains with such premises until the inspection is made
by the Superintendent and the work of the plumbing is satisfactory to him.
('79 Code, § 17-52)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.031 INFORMATION TO BE SUBMITTED AFTER INSPECTION AND APPROVAL.
   (A)   Within 48 hours after the work described in §
52.030 has been inspected and found satisfactory by the Superintendent of the
Waterworks, the plumber shall make out on a blank furnished him by the city, an
accurate return to the Superintendent setting out the location of the premises
in reference to the street on which the same fronts, the number of the house,
if any, the name of the owner or occupant of the premises, and in plain writing
all the uses, both ordinary and special, to which the water is designed to be
applied; the failure on the part of any plumber to do so shall be grounds to
revoke his certificate of registration.
   (B)   The plumber shall in no case be allowed to deliver such return to the
owner or occupant of the premises, but must in all cases deliver the same to
the Superintendent.
('79 Code, § 17-53)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.032 CONSUMER TO MAINTAIN STOP BOX; LIABILITY FOR FAILURE TO PROVIDE
ACCESS.
   The consumer of city water shall at all times use care to see that the stop
box is kept in good repair, and in plain view, and access to the stop box not
in any manner obstructed. If it is not so arranged and the city has to dig up
the main to shut off the water or to turn it on, the property owner shall be
liable for and chargeable with the extra expense, including that of digging and
excavating.
('79 Code, § 17-54)
§ 52.033 INSPECTIONS BY SUPERINTENDENT; CONTROL OF STOPCOCK.
   The Superintendent of the Waterworks Department shall have access to and be
permitted at any reasonable time to inspect all pipes, fixtures and apparatus
supplied with water service, and shall have the power to control the stopcock
in the cellar as the interests of the city may require.
('79 Code, § 17-55)
§ 52.034 FORFEITURE OR REVOCATION OF REGISTRATION OF PLUMBER.
   (A)   In addition to any other penalty provided by law, any plumber
violating the bylaws, rules or regulations which have been established by the
city for the government of the waterworks shall forfeit his registration; and
upon the discovery of any such violation the Mayor shall immediately revoke his
registration and the plumber will be prohibited from doing any further work in
connection with the waterworks until full satisfaction has been rendered in the
way of paying all penalties prescribed by the bylaws for such violation and
satisfactory assurance given that in the future no violations of the bylaws,
rules or regulations of the waterworks will be committed by the plumber and
until his registration has been reinstated by the Mayor.
   (B)   The forfeiture or revocation of the registration of any plumber who is
a member of or employed by a corporation or firm, shall operate as to affect
all other members of the firm or corporation alike, and no separate
registration shall be issued to any person interested in or employed by the
firm or corporation so long as the offending plumber is a member of or employed
by the firm or corporation.
('79 Code, § 17-56)
§ 52.035 CROSS CONNECTIONS.
   (A)   A cross connection shall be defined as any physical connection or
arrangement between two otherwise separate systems, one of which contains
potable water from the city water system, and the other, water from a private
source, water of unknown or questionable safety, or steam, gases, or chemicals,
whereby there may be a flow from one system to the other, the direction of flow
depending on the pressure differential between the two systems.
   (B)   No person, firm, or corporation shall establish or permit to be
established or maintain or permit to be maintained any cross connection. No
interconnection shall be established whereby potable water from a private,
auxiliary, or emergency water supply and the method of connection and use of
such supply shall have been approved by the Department of Water Works and by
the state Department of Environmental Management in accordance with 327 IAC 8-
10.
   (C)   It shall be the duty of the Water Works Department to cause inspection
to be made of all properties served by the public water system where cross
connections with the public water system is deemed possible.
      (1)   The frequency of inspections and reinspection based on potential
health hazards involved shall be established by the Water Works Department.
      (2)   Upon presentation of credentials, the representative of the Water
Works Department shall have the right to request entry at any reasonable time
to examine the property served by a connection to the public water system of
the city for cross connections. On request, the owner, lessee, or occupant of
any property so served, shall furnish to the inspection agency any pertinent
information regarding the piping systems on such property. The refusal of
access or refusal of requested pertinent information shall be deemed evidence
of the presence of cross connections.
      (3)   The Department of Water Works is hereby authorized and directed to
discontinue water service to any property wherein any connection in violation
of this section exists, and to take such other precautionary measures deemed
necessary to eliminate any danger of contamination of the public water system.
Water service shall not be restored until the cross connection(s) has been
eliminated in compliance with the provisions of this subchapter. If it is
deemed by the Department of Water Works that a cross connection or an emergency
endangers public health, safety, or welfare and requires immediate action, and
a written finding to that effect is filed with the Clerk and delivered to the
consumer’s premises, service may be immediately discontinued. The consumer
shall have an opportunity for a hearing within ten days of such emergency
discontinuance.
   (D)   All consumers using toxic or hazardous liquids, all hospitals,
mortuaries, wastewater treatment plants, laboratories, and all other hazardous
users shall install and maintain a reduced-pressure-principal backflow
preventer in the main water line serving each building on the premises. The
backflow preventor must be installed in an easily accessible location not
subject to flooding or freezing.
   (E)   That all consumers determined by the Indiana Department of
Environmental Management (IDEM) as high hazard by using toxic or hazardous
liquids, which includes:
      (1)   Aircraft and missile manufacturing plants;
      (2)   Automotive plants;
      (3)   Beverage bottling plants, including dairies and breweries;
      (4)   Canneries, packing houses and reduction plants;
      (5)   Car washes;
      (6)   Chemical, biological, radiological laboratories, including those in
high schools, trade schools, colleges, universities and research institutions;
      (7)   Hospitals, clinics, medical buildings, autopsy facilities, morgues,
medical facilities and mortuaries;
      (8)   Metal and plastic manufacturing, fabricating, cleaning, plating and
processing facilities;
      (9)   Plants manufacturing paper and paper products;
      (10)   Plants manufacturing, refining, compounding, or processing
fertilizer, film, herbicides, natural or synthetic rubber, pesticides,
petroleum products, pharmaceuticals, radiological materials, or any chemical
that could be a contaminant to the public water supply;
      (11)   Commercial facilities that use herbicides, pesticides,
fertilizers, or any chemical that could be a contaminant to the public water
supply;
      (12)   Plants processing, blending, or refining animal, vegetable or
mineral oils;
      (13)   Commercial laundries and dye works, including coin-operated
laundromats;
      (14)   Sewage, storm water and industrial waste treatment plants and
pumping stations;
      (15)   Waterfront facilities, including piers, docks, marinas and
shipyards;
      (16)   Industrial facilities that recycle water;
      (17)   Restricted or classified facilities (federal government defense or
military installations), or other facilities closed to the supplier of water or
to the Commissioner;
      (18)   Private water wells connected to the municipal water system;
      (19)   Irrigation systems;
      (20)   Any other application deemed a risk to the public water supply as
determined by the City of Rochester Water Department.
   (F)   The reduced pressure principle backflow preventers shall not be
installed below ground level. All reduced pressure principle backflow
preventers must be installed in an easily accessible location not subject to
flooding or freezing as approved by the City of Rochester Water Department.
   (G)   This section does not supersede the Indiana Plumbing Code, the IDEM
Rule 327 IAC 8-10 or the city plumbing ordinances, but it supplementary to
them.
   (H)   If, in the judgment of the Superintendent of Water, an approved
backflow prevention device is necessary for the safety of the public water
system, the Superintendent of Water will give notice to the water consumer to
install such an approved device immediately. The water consumer shall, at his
or her own expense, install such an approved device at a location and in a
manner approved by the Superintendent of Water and shall have inspections and
test made of such approved devices as required by the Superintendent of Water
and in accordance with the IDEM Rule 327 IAC 8-10.
(Ord. 31-1999, passed 11-9-99; Am. Ord. 09-2016, passed 9-6-16)
METERS
§ 52.045 SERVICE TO BE METERED; PERMIT TO REMOVE METER.
   All services for the furnishing of water to any consumer shall be measured
by a meter which shall be furnished by the Waterworks Department and no person
shall interfere with or remove any water meter from any service line after it
has been attached unless upon the written permit of the Superintendent;
provided, however, that service furnished for public and private fire
protection shall not be required to be metered.
('79 Code, § 17-72)
Cross-reference:
   
Adjustments for meter leakage, see § 52.103
   
Testing of meters to determine overcharge, see § 52.105
§ 52.046 BOARD TO SPECIFY SIZE AND TYPE OF METER.
   The Board of Waterworks Trustees shall specify the size and type of water
meter required by the service to be performed.
('79 Code, § 17-73)
§ 52.047 OBSTRUCTION OF METERS; SHUTTING OFF WATER FOR VIOLATION; RIGHT OF CITY
TO EXAMINE METERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to cover up, or in any way obstruct, the
free access to any water meter in the service of the Waterworks Department. In
case of violation of this provision on the part of the owner or tenant, and
failure on the part of the owner or tenant to remove such obstructions upon
notice from the Superintendent of the Waterworks Department, the water service
shall be immediately shut off from the premises; the city reserves the right to
examine every meter connected to the waterworks system, whether located for
convenience on private property or in any public street or alley.
('79 Code, § 17-74)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.048 REMOVAL OF WATER METER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person not employed by the Waterworks
Department, or not a licensed plumber working by permission of the Waterworks
Department, to attach or remove a water meter to or from any service pipe
connected to the waterworks system.
('79 Code, § 17-75)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 52.049 OUTSIDE METER INSTALLATIONS.
   Whenever a water meter is installed outside of a building, it shall be
installed in a pit which meets with the approval of the Waterworks Department.
The pit shall be not less than 20 inches in diameter and not less than four
feet in depth with a cast-iron cover as approved by the Department. All meters
shall be raised within 18 inches of the top of the meter box pit. Where it is
necessary to install outside meters the costs of such installation shall be
borne by the consumer. Where a meter is located on the inside of a building the
consumer shall be responsible for any damage that occurs to the meter when
damage has occurred, and upon notification thereof the Department will repair
or replace any such meter but will make a charge to the consumer to cover the
costs of materials and labor in case of repair or to cover the new meter in
case a new meter is furnished.
('79 Code, § 17-76)

three Directors, which Directors shall serve for terms of three years,

appointed for terms of one year, two years, and three years respectively so as

WATERWORKS BONDS; DISPOSITION OF REVENUE
§ 52.080 KEEPING OF RECORDS; INSPECTION BY BOND HOLDERS.
   The city shall keep proper books and records, separate from all other
records and accounts, in which complete and correct entries shall be made
showing all revenues collected from the waterworks system and deposited in the
special fund hereinafter established, and all disbursements made therefrom,
together with all transactions, relating to the system. The city, upon request,
shall furnish to any holder of any of its waterworks bonds, not more than 30
days after the close of each six months fiscal period, complete operating and
income statements of the system in reasonable detail covering the six-month
period, and not more than 60 days after the close of the fiscal year, shall
furnish complete financial statements of the waterworks system, and of the city
covering such fiscal year and certified by the Clerk-Treasurer. The financial
statements of the waterworks system shall at all times be kept on file in the
office of the Clerk-Treasurer. Any holder of any of the bonds shall have the
right at all reasonable times to inspect the waterworks system and all records,
accounts and data of the city relating thereto.
('79 Code, § 17-25)
§ 52.081 DUTIES OF CLERK-TREASURER; HANDLING OF FUNDS.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the Clerk-Treasurer to receive all moneys from
the Cashier as provided in § 52.006 and all other revenues arising from the
operation of the waterworks and keep the revenues in separate and distinct
funds as hereinafter designated and all warrants for claims and other
indebtedness against the fund shall be signed by the Clerk-Treasurer.
   (B)   All funds belonging to the waterworks shall be deposited in the
regular depository of the city in separate accounts from other city funds and
the separate accounts shall be designated:
      (1)   Waterworks fund;
      (2)   Meter deposit fund;
      (3)   Bond and interest redemption fund;
      (4)   Depreciation fund; and
      (5)   Such other funds as from time to time may be required.
   (C)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall also keep appropriate records of the various
transactions pertaining to the waterworks including a record of appropriations
as the they are made by the Common Council.
   (D)   The City Clerk-Treasurer’s Office is authorized to accept a credit
card or debit card for payment of water / waste water utility bills. In the
event of a charge to the city for the use of the credit or debit card payments,
the City Clerk-Treasurer’s Office is authorized and directed to charge and
collect a sum equal to the amount of the charge from the person who uses the
credit or debit card for payment of their water / waste water utility bill.
(‘79 Code, § 17-28) (Am. Ord. 17-2008, passed 1-13-09)
RATES AND CHARGES
§ 52.095 DUTY OF CITY TO ESTABLISH JUST RATES.
   The city shall establish, maintain and collect nondiscriminatory,
reasonable, and just rates or charges for the facilities and service afforded
by its waterworks system which shall be sufficient to:
   (A)   Pay the legal and other necessary expenses incident to the operation
of the utility, including maintenance costs, operating charges, upkeep,
repairs, depreciation, interest charges on bonds and other obligations,
including leases, and costs associated with the acquisition of utility property
under I.C. 8-1.5-2;
   (B)   Provide a sinking fund for the liquidation of bonds or other
obligations, including leases;
   (C)   Provide a debt service reserve for bonds or other obligations,
including leases, in an amount not to exceed the maximum annual debt service on
the bonds or obligations or the maximum annual lease rentals;
   (D)   Provide adequate money for working capital;
   (E)   Provide adequate money for making extensions and replacements to the
extent not provided for through depreciation in division (A) above; and
   (F)   Provide money for the payment of any taxes that may be assessed
against the utility.
(‘79 Code, § 17-64) (Am. Ord. 10-1021, passed 8-24-21)
Statutory reference:
   Rates and charges, see I.C. 8-1.5-3-8

waterworks of the city, except as otherwise may be provided by contract, the
rates and services listed in this subchapter, based upon the amount of water
supplied during each monthly water billing period.

§ 52.099 HYDRANT CHARGES; PRIVATE HYDRANTS.
   (A)   Hydrant charges. The annual charge for water service shall be as
follows:
      Municipal hydrants   $300 per hydrant
      Private hydrants   $300 per hydrant
   (B)   Private fire hydrants. All private fire hydrants within the city shall
be located, installed and maintained in accordance with the following:
      (1)   Costs for the installation and maintenance of a private fire
hydrant, as detailed in this section, shall be the responsibility of the
property owner.
      (2)   All private fire hydrants shall be installed in accordance with
nationally recognized good practices, NFPA Standards, AWWA Standards and by the
city Water Department specifications maintained with the building fire
protection system.
      (3)   All private fire hydrants must be the color red and the large
diameter steamer connection shall be a five-inch Storz fitting. The two smaller
connections shall be two and one-half-inch male (NST) National Standard
Threads. All private fire hydrants shall have an approved shut-off valve
installed in the fire hydrant lead not more than 100 feet from the fire
hydrant. Such shut-off valve shall be accessible at all times.
      (4)   All private fire hydrant placement must be approved by the city
Water Department and the Fire Chief before installation, and accessible at all
times for fire-fighting purposes. No private fire hydrant shall be installed
closer than two feet or more than five feet from a street, roadway or driveway.
For average conditions, all private fire hydrants shall be placed 50 feet from
the building protected, as specified by the authority having jurisdiction. All
private fire hydrants shall be set plumb with outlets a minimum of 18 inches
above the adjoining finished grade.
      (5)   All private fire hydrants are required to be inspected and tested
once per year by a qualified testing company to verify the flow, proper
operation, and should consist of greasing outlets and greasing stem. The
results must include the hydrant location and the results of the flow test
(static pressure and GMP flow). The property owner will maintain a copy of the
test certification on the premises and send a copy within 30 days of the
testing to the city Water Department at 320 Main Street, Rochester, Indiana
46975.
      (6)   All private fire hydrants shall be maintained in proper working
order by the owner and must be repaired or replaced within 180 days if non-
conforming.
      (7)   Notification must be made to the Fire Department of any private
fire hydrant taken out or service for repair or maintenance and reported back
in service to the Fire Department when repaired by calling the Fire Department
during normal business hours.
(‘79 Code, § 17-68) (Ord. 491, passed 11-25-69; Am. Ord. 796, passed 4-22-80;
Am. Ord. 111-1987, passed 11-10-87; Am. Ord. 8-1990, passed 4-10-90; Am. Ord.
22-1993, passed 12-28-93; Am. Ord. 19-2001, passed 11-13-01; Am. Ord. 21-2004,
passed 10-26-04; Am. Ord. 12-2009, passed 9-23-09; Am. Ord. 10-2021, passed 8-

   All bills for water services not paid within 15 days from the billing due
date thereof, as stated on the bills, shall be subject to a collection or
deferred payment charge of 10% on the first $3 and 3% on the excess over $3.
(‘79 Code, § 17-71) (Ord. 491, passed 11-25-69; Am. Ord. 111-1987, passed 11-

§ 52.103 ADJUSTMENTS FOR METER LEAKAGE.
   If a water meter fails to register correctly, the bill for water used shall
be estimated from the most recent date as the Superintendent of the Waterworks
Department and the Board of Directors shall determine, but no deductions will
be made from the bill on account of leakage, and no adjustment will be made on
any bill by reason of any leak that occurs inside of a building.
('79 Code, § 17-78)
Cross-reference:
   
Meters, see §§ 52.045 et seq.
§ 52.104 DISCONNECTION OF SERVICE FOR NONPAYMENT.
   (A)   When the Water Board orders the water of any consumer shut off for
nonpayment of charges, the supply shall not again be turned on until the
consumer shall pay all charges due and in addition pay a turn-on charge in the
sum of $50. However, this sum shall be $75 if the consumer’s service has been
shut off one time in the previous 12 months and $200 if the consumer has been
shut off two or more times in the previous 12 months. The delinquency
hereinbefore mentioned shall be held and construed to mean any and all bills
due the waterworks from the consumer whether the bills shall arise from the
occupancy of the same or different premises.
   (B)   The past due notice threshold shall be $10.
   (C)   Upon learning that an account exists in the name of a deceased
consumer, the Water Department may send a letter to the occupant(s) of the
property receiving service, notifying the occupant(s) that service will be
disconnected if a new account is not created for service to the property within
a reasonable time, as determined by the Water Board.
(‘79 Code, § 17-80) (Ord. 931, passed 12-14-82; Am. Ord. 951, passed 7-26-83;
Am. Ord. 23-1989, passed 6-13-89; Am. Ord. 09-2006, passed 8-22-06; Am. Ord.
13-2013, passed 4-23-13; Am. Ord. 03-2019, passed 5-28-19; Am. Ord. 10-2021,
passed 8-24-21)
§ 52.105 TESTING OF METERS TO DETERMINE OVERCHARGE.
   (A)   Whenever any customer of the Waterworks Department believes that he is
being overcharged for water service and wishes to have the water meter serving
him tested, the customer will be entitled to have his water meter tested by
making a written request to the Water Department for the meter testing.
   (B)   Upon receiving such written request, the Water Department shall make
appropriate arrangements for the transportation of the water meter and the
testing thereof at an appropriate testing laboratory.
   (C)   In the event that after testing any such water meter is 95% correct,
the costs for transportation and testing for the water meter shall be paid by
the customer requesting the testing; and the amount for transportation and
testing of the water meter shall be added to the water bill for that customer.
   (D)   In the event that after testing the water meter is erroneous by more
than 5%, the cost of the transportation and testing of the water meter shall be
paid by the Water Department; and the Department shall install an accurate
water meter for service to the customer.
   (E)   In the event that the water meter proves to be more than 5% in error,
any adjustment to be made for water service to the customer requesting the
testing shall be limited to a period of one year immediately prior to the
testing of the water meter.
('79 Code, § 17-81) (Ord. 15-1990, passed 7-10-90)
Cross-reference:
   
Meters, see §§ 52.045 et seq.

§ 52.119 CONNECTION FEE FOR EXISTING BUILDINGS; EXCEPTIONS.
   The owner of any building existing on November 1, 1987, which connects to
the water utility shall, prior to being permitted to make such connection, pay
a connection fee in the amount of $3,000 per equivalent single-family dwelling
unit as calculated under §
52.116 hereof for the property to be served by the connection. Provided,
however, no connection fee will be required of any such owner connecting to a
water service line if the following conditions are met:
   (A)   The connection takes place within 90 days of the date on which water
becomes available for connection; and
   (B)   The owner pays the debt surcharge as set forth in §
52.116 hereof.
('79 Code, § 17-88) (Ord. 112-1987, passed 11-10-87)
§ 52.120 CONNECTION FEE FOR NEWER BUILDINGS; EXCEPTIONS.
   The owner of any building which is not in existence on November 1, 1987, but
which comes into existence prior to the completion of the water distribution
system as per the plans and designs of Philip L. Schnelker, Inc., Consulting
Engineer, including platted lots, and wishes to connect to the water utility,
shall, prior to being permitted to make connection, pay a connection fee in the
amount of $3,000 per equivalent single-family dwelling unit as calculated under
§
52.116 hereof for the property to be served by the connection. Provided,
however, no connection fee will be required of any such owner connecting to a
water service line if the following conditions are met:
   (A)   The connection takes place before the later of the date of January 1,
1989, or date on which water becomes available for connection;
   (B)   The owner pays the debt surcharge as set forth in §
52.116 hereof retroactive to the beginning of the construction process; and
   (C)   That the owner pays the standard water tap fee as provided by other
city ordinance.
('79 Code, § 17-89) (Ord. 112-1987, passed 11-10-87)
§ 52.121 OPTIONS AVAILABLE TO OWNERS OF UNDEVELOPED PROPERTY ABUTTING WATER
SERVICE LINE.
   (A)   The owners of undeveloped property abutting the water service line as
per the plans and designs of Philip L. Schnelker, Inc., Consulting Engineer,
may, prior to January 1, 1989, elect one of the following options:
      (1)   Pay the connection charge of $3,000. Pursuant to such payment, the
water service line will be extended to the owner's property line. Upon future
development of the property and connection to the water system, the owner will
be entitled to one equivalent single-family dwelling unit as calculated under §
52.116 hereof without payment of additional connection fee.
      (2)   Pay the monthly surcharge of $20 as set forth in §
52.116 hereof. Upon future development of the property and connection to the
water system, the owner will be entitled to one equivalent single-family
dwelling unit as calculated under §
52.116 hereof without payment of additional connection fee, provided, however,
no connection may be made unless the surcharge payments are current.
   (B)   In addition, the owner shall pay the standard water tap fee as
provided by other city ordinance.
('79 Code, § 17-90) (Ord. 112-1987, passed 11-10-87)

§ 70.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this title, the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ALLEY. A public thoroughfare which affords only secondary means of vehicular
access to abutting property and not over 20 feet in width.
   CENTRAL FIRE DISTRICT. All streets and portions of streets within the fire
limits.
   COMMERCIAL VEHICLE. Every vehicle designed, maintained, or used primarily
for the transportation of property.
   CURB LOADING ZONE. A space adjacent to a curb reserved for the exclusive use
of vehicles during the loading or unloading of passengers or materials.
   FREIGHT CURB LOADING ZONE. A space adjacent to a curb for the exclusive use
of vehicles during the loading or unloading of freight or passengers.
   PARK. The standing of a vehicle, whether occupied or not, otherwise than
temporarily for the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or
unloading.
   PASSENGER CURB LOADING ZONE. A place adjacent to a curb reserved for the
exclusive use of vehicles during the loading or unloading of passengers.
   STOP. The complete cessation of movement.
   STOP, STOPPING, or STANDING. Any stopping or standing of a vehicle, whether
occupied or not, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or
in compliance with the directions of a police officer or traffic-control sign
or signal.
('79 Code, § 8-1)
Statutory reference:
   State traffic definitions generally, see I.C. 9-13-2-1 et seq.
§ 70.02 COMPLIANCE REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to do any act forbidden or to fail to
perform any act required by this title.
('79 Code, § 8-2)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 70.03 OBEDIENCE TO POLICE AND FIRE DEPARTMENT OFFICIALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully fail or refuse to comply
with any lawful order or direction of a police officer or Fire Department
official.
('79 Code, § 8-3)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 70.04 PERSONS EXEMPT FROM TITLE; AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES.
   (A)   The provisions of this title applicable to the drivers of all vehicles
owned or operated by the United States, this state or any county, city, town,
district, or any other political subdivision of the state, subject to such
specific exceptions as are set forth in this title with reference to authorized
emergency vehicles.
   (B)   Unless specifically made applicable, the provisions of this title
shall not apply to persons, teams, motor vehicles and other equipment while
actually engaged in work on the surface of a highway but shall apply to such
persons and vehicles when traveling to or from work.
   (C)   The driver of any authorized emergency vehicle when responding to an
emergency call or when in the pursuit of an actual or suspected violator of the
law or when responding, but not upon returning from a fire alarm, may exercise
the privileges set forth in this title but subject to the conditions herein
stated.
   (D)   The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle may:
      (1)   Park or stand, irrespective of the provisions of this title.
      (2)   Proceed past a red or stop signal or stop sign, but only after
slowing down as may be necessary for safe operation.
      (3)   Exceed the maximum speed limits so long as he does not endanger
life or property.
      (4)   Disregard regulations governing direction of movement or turning in
specified directions.
   (E)   The exemptions herein granted to an authorized emergency vehicle shall
apply only when the vehicle is making use of audible and visual signals meeting
the requirements of law, except that an authorized emergency vehicle operated
as a police vehicle need not be equipped with or display a red light visible
from in front of the vehicle.
   (F)   The foregoing provisions shall not relieve the driver of an authorized
emergency vehicle from the duty to drive with due regard for the safety of all
persons, nor shall such provisions protect the driver from the consequences of
his reckless disregard for the safety of others.
('79 Code, § 8-5)
Penalty, see § 70.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see I.C. 9-21-1-6 through 9-21-1-8
§ 70.05 SIDEWALK/TRAFFIC SAFETY COMMISSION.
   (A)   There is hereby established a commission to be entitled and designated
as the “Rochester Sidewalk/Traffic Safety Advisory Commission.”
   (B)   (1)   The Commission shall consist of nine members, four being
officials of the city and five non-officials. No member shall be paid or
granted any salary or compensation from the city. The four official members
shall consist of representatives from:
         (a)   The Police Department;
         (b)   The Fire Department;
         (c)   The Street Department; and
         (d)   The Common Council.
      (2)   The representative of the Common Council shall serve as Chairperson
of the Commission.
   (C)   The members of the Commission shall be appointed by the Mayor upon the
recommendation of the Common Council and shall serve until their successors are
appointed.
   (D)   The President of the Board of Public Works and Safety shall serve as
an ex officio member without a vote. The Commission is authorized to appoint as
ex officio members of the Commission any additional members without voting
privileges by majority vote of the Commission at any meeting where a quorum is
present.
   (E)   The Chairperson of the Commission shall appoint the Secretary of the
Commission who shall have the duty to:
      (1)   Send all notices for the meetings of the Commission;
      (2)   Keep and preserve the minutes; have custody and keep all documents
and papers filed with the Commission; and
      (3)   Perform such other duties as may be prescribed by the Commission.
   (F)   The Commission shall meet on the call of its Chairman or on call by a
majority of its members. Five members shall constitute a quorum.
   (G)   The responsibilities of the Commission shall include, but not be
limited to, the following:
      (1)   Developing and implementing coordinated sidewalk and traffic safety
programs which meet local needs;
      (2)   Acting in an advisory capacity to the Common Council in the
coordination of traffic safety activities of the official agencies of the city;
      (3)   Establishing sidewalk and traffic safety priorities for the city;
      (4)   Reviewing and approving project applications for funding;
      (5)   Serving in a liaison capacity between the city and the Indiana
Department of Traffic Safety in developing the state highway safety program and
in meeting the national Highway Safety Program Standards;
      (6)   Promoting public acceptance of official programs proposed or
instigated by the city;
      (7)   Fostering public knowledge and support of traffic law enforcement
and traffic engineering problems;
      (8)   Cooperating with the schools in promoting educational pedestrian
and traffic safety aids;
      (9)   Educating the public in pedestrian and traffic safety;
      (10)   Generally aiding the overall reduction of accidents, injuries and
deaths on the city streets and sidewalks.
      (11)   Advise and consult with the Board of Public Works and Safety and
city officials as to the work and recommendations of the Commission; and
      (12)   Work with organized community groups and others to carry forward
all plans and policies of the Commission as to accident prevention which may be
approved by the Commission.
(‘79 Code, § 8-5.1) (Ord. 714, passed 4-11-78; Am. Ord. 04-2001, passed 2-27-
01; Am. Ord. 01-2012, passed 2-28-12)
§ 70.06 DISPOSITION OF TRAFFIC FINES AND FORFEITURES.
   (A)   All fines or forfeitures collected upon conviction or upon the
forfeiture of bail of any person charged with a violation of any of the
provisions of this title shall be paid into the city treasury as required by
law.
   (B)   The failure, refusal, or neglect on the part of any judicial or other
officer or employee receiving or having custody of any traffic fine or
forfeiture, either before or after its deposit in the street and traffic safety
improvement fund to comply with division (A) shall constitute misconduct in
office and shall be ground for removal therefrom.
('79 Code, § 8-31)
Statutory reference:
   Disposition of fines assessed for traffic violations, see I.C. 9-21-1-2
§ 70.07 INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE OF SIGNS, SIGNALS, AND THE LIKE.
   The Police Department shall place and maintain traffic-control signs,
signals and devices when required under all traffic ordinances and when
necessary to make such ordinances effective.
('79 Code, § 8-32)
§ 70.08 SPECIAL PROVISIONS FOR SCHOOL PROPERTY.
   (A)   All traffic regulations of the state and the city shall be enforceable
by officers of the Police Department of the city with regard to all motor
vehicles, drivers and occupants thereof which shall be operated or found upon
the property of the Rochester Community School Corporation; it shall be
unlawful to violate the traffic regulations.
   (B)   The speed limit for all motorized vehicles on school drives and access
roadways shall be as posted by appropriate sign, but not to exceed 25 miles per
hour. The speed limit for all motorized vehicles on other school property,
including parking lot areas shall not exceed 15 miles per hour.
   (C)   All regular and appropriate directional signs, including stop, yield
and one-way signs shall be complied with and enforced in the same manner as if
placed upon the streets and highways of the city and state.
   (D)   No unauthorized vehicles shall be permitted off of the roadways on
school properties.
   (E)   The operations of snowmobiles, go-carts, off-the-road vehicles and all
other similar motorized vehicles on school property is prohibited.
   (F)   Driving or parking on school property shall be limited to those
vehicles operated by individuals who are attending school or school functions,
on official school business, or participating in approved recreational
activities on the school site or property.
('79 Code, § 8-27.1) (Ord. 674, passed 1-26-77)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 70.09 SPECIAL PROVISIONS FOR ROCHESTER PLAZA SHOPPING CENTER PROPERTY.
   (A)   All traffic regulations of the state and the city shall be enforced by
officers of the Police Department of the city with regard to all motor
vehicles, drivers, and occupants thereof, which shall be operated upon or found
upon the property of Rochester Plaza Shopping Center. It shall be unlawful to
violate any of the ordinances of the city concerning traffic regulations or any
statutes of the State of Indiana concerning traffic regulations on the
property.
   (B)   The speed limit for all motorized vehicles on Rochester Plaza Shopping
Center property shall be limited as may be hereafter posted by any appropriate
signs but in any event shall not exceed 15 miles per hour on the property.
   (C)   All appropriate directional signs and all stop, yield, or one-way
signs which shall be properly placed upon the property shall be complied with
and enforced in the same manner as if placed upon the streets and highways of
the city.
   (D)   The operation of snowmobiles, go-carts, off-the-road vehicles and all
other similar motorized vehicles on the property of Rochester Plaza Shopping
Center is prohibited.
   (E)   Driving or parking on Rochester Plaza Shopping Center property shall
be limited to those vehicles operated by persons who are shopping or otherwise
transacting business with a tenant or business occupant of Rochester Plaza
Shopping Center.
('79 Code, § 8-27.2) (Ord. 80-1986, passed 12-30-86)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 70.10 SPECIAL PROVISIONS FOR PEACE TREE PLAZA SHOPPING CENTER PROPERTY.
   (A)   All traffic regulations of the state and city shall be enforced by
officers of the Police Department of the city with regard to all motor
vehicles, drivers, and occupants thereof, which shall be operated upon or found
upon the property of Peace Tree Shopping Center. It shall be unlawful to
violate any of the ordinances of the city concerning traffic regulations or any
statutes of the State of Indiana concerning traffic regulations on the
property.
   (B)   The speed limit for all motorized vehicles on Peace Tree Shopping
Center property shall be limited as may be hereafter posted by any appropriate
signs but in any event shall not exceed 15 miles per hour on the property.
   (C)   All appropriate directional signs and all stop, yield or one-way signs
which shall be properly placed upon the property shall be complied with and
enforced in the same manner as if placed upon the streets and highways of the
city.
   (D)   Operation of snowmobiles, go-carts, off-the-road vehicles and all
other similar motorized vehicles on the property of Peace Tree Shopping Center
is prohibited.
   (E)   Driving or parking on Peace Tree Shopping Center property shall be
limited to those vehicles operated by persons who are shopping or otherwise
transacting business with a tenant or business occupant of Peace Tree Shopping
Center.
(Ord. 32-1997, passed 9-23-97)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Unless another penalty is expressly provided, whoever violates any
provision of this title and any other traffic ordinance of the city shall be
punished as provided for in §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   The penalty for violating §
70.08 shall be that imposed by the laws of the state or the city with regard to
the particular violation committed; provided, however, for any violation, the
Commission of which has not been unlawful under prior statute or ordinance,
upon conviction, the violator shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $500.
('79 Code, § 8-27.1) (Ord. 674, passed 1-26-77)
   (C)   The penalty for violating §
70.09 shall be that imposed by the laws of the state or the city with regard to
the particular violation committed; provided, however, for any violation, the
Commission of which has not been unlawful under prior statute or ordinance,
upon conviction, the violator shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $500.
('79 Code, § 8-27.2) (Ord. 80-1986, passed 12-30-86)
