§ 71.01 TURNING AROUND.
   It shall be unlawful for the driver of any vehicle to turn the vehicle so as
to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street in a business district, or
upon any other street so turn a vehicle unless such movement can be made in
safety and without interfering with other traffic.
('79 Code, § 8-7)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.02 DRIVING ON SIDEWALKS.
   It shall be unlawful for the driver of a motor vehicle to drive within any
sidewalk area except at a permanent or temporary driveway.
('79 Code, § 8-10)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.03 RESTRICTION ON CERTAIN COMMERCIAL VEHICLES IN RESIDENCE DISTRICTS.
   Except on state highways or state-controlled highways it shall be unlawful
for any person to operate a commercial vehicle with a gross weight in excess of
10,000 pounds in any residence district; provided, however, that this
prohibition shall not apply to such a vehicle when it is making a delivery from
a state or state-controlled highway and returning to it by the most direct
route possible, and in the event that this restriction results in any undue
hardship or unfair competition, the Chief of Police shall have the power to
authorize the issuance of special permits from time to time as deemed necessary
for the protection of the rights of any individual.
('79 Code, § 8-11) (Ord. 577, passed 11-27-73)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.04 MANNER OF CONDUCTING PROCESSIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for a driver in a funeral or other procession to fail
to drive as near to the right-hand edge of the roadway as practical, or to fail
to follow the vehicle ahead of it as closely as is practical and safe.
('79 Code, § 8-12)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.05 USE OF PLAY STREETS.
   Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating any street or part thereof
as a play street, no person shall drive a vehicle upon any such street or
portion thereof except for drivers of vehicles having business or whose
residences are within the closed area, and then any said driver shall exercise
the greatest care in driving upon any such street or portion thereof.
('79 Code, § 8-14)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.06 OBSTRUCTION OF INTERSECTIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any driver,except the driver of a school bus, to
enter an intersection or a marked crosswalk unless there is sufficient space on
the other side of it to accommodate the vehicle he is operating without
obstructing the passage of other vehicles or pedestrians, notwithstanding any
traffic-control signal indication to proceed.
('79 Code, § 8-19) (Ord. 13-1997, passed 7-8-97)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 71.07 ANGLE LOADING OR UNLOADING PERMIT.
   The Chief of Police is hereby authorized to issue special permits for the
backing of a vehicle to the curb for the purpose of loading or unloading
merchandise or materials subject to the terms and conditions of the permit. The
permits may be issued either to the owner or lessee of real property or to the
owner of the vehicle and shall grant to the person the privilege as therein
stated and authorized herein, and it shall be unlawful for any permittee or
other person to violate any of the special terms or conditions of any such
permit.
('79 Code, § 8-20)
Penalty, see § 70.99
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
General Provisions
   
72.01   Parking to display, wash, grease or repair vehicle
   
72.02   Parking in alleys
   
72.03   Use of bus and cab stands by other vehicles
   
72.04   Presumption with reference to illegal parking
   
72.05   Impoundment of vehicles
Buses; Taxicabs
   
72.15   Stopping, standing or parking buses
   
72.16   Stopping, standing or parking of taxicabs
Handicapped Parking Spaces
   
72.20   Application
   
72.21   Authority of police
   
72.22   Parking fees and fines
   
72.23   Definitions
   
72.24   Parking for persons with a physical challenge required
   
72.25   Parking for persons with a physical challenge
   
72.26   Compliance with state law required
   
72.27   Exclusiveness of state parking permits
   
72.28   Reciprocity
   
72.29   Enforcement
   
72.30   Violations
   
72.31   Penalty
   
72.32   Supremacy clause
Statutory reference:
   Power of city to regulate parking generally, see I.C. 9-21-1-3(a)(1)
Cross-reference:
   Off-street parking, see §
152.044
   Special provisions for school property, see §
70.08
   Special provisions for Rochester Plaza Shopping Center property, see §
70.09
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 72.01 PARKING TO DISPLAY, WASH, GREASE OR REPAIR VEHICLE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle upon any street or
highway for the principal purpose of displaying it for sale, or washing,
greasing, or repairing the vehicle; provided, however, that this section shall
not be construed to prohibit parking to make repairs necessitated by an
emergency.
('79 Code, § 8-23)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 72.02 PARKING IN ALLEYS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle within an alley in
such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet
of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic, or to
stop, stand, or park a vehicle within an alley in such position as to block the
driveway entrance to any abutting property.
('79 Code, § 8-24)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 72.03 USE OF BUS AND CAB STANDS BY OTHER VEHICLES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to stop, stand, or park a vehicle other
than a bus in a bus stop, or other than a taxicab in a taxicab stand, except
that the driver of a passenger vehicle may temporarily stop therein for the
purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers when
the stopping does not interfere with any bus or taxicab waiting to enter or
about to enter the zone.
('79 Code, § 8-27)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 72.04 PRESUMPTION WITH REFERENCE TO ILLEGAL PARKING.
   In any prosecution for illegal standing or parking of a vehicle proof that
the particular vehicle described in the complaint was illegally parked together
with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was at the time of the
parking the registered owner of the vehicle, shall constitute in evidence a
prima facie presumption that the registered owner of the vehicle was the person
who parked or placed the vehicle at the point where, and for the time during
which, the violation occurred; provided, however, that the provisions of this
section shall apply only when the proper arrest and citation procedure has been
followed.
('79 Code, § 8-28)
Statutory reference:
   Arrest and citation procedure generally, see I.C. 9-30-2-1 et seq.
§ 72.05 IMPOUNDMENT OF VEHICLES.
   (A)   Members of the Police Department are hereby authorized to remove a
vehicle from a street or highway to the nearest garage or other place of
safety, or to a garage designated or maintained by the city located in or
within one mile of the city limits under the following circumstances:
      (1)   When any vehicle is left unattended upon any bridge or in any
tunnel where the vehicle constitutes an obstruction to traffic.
      (2)   When a vehicle upon a highway is so disabled as to constitute an
obstruction to traffic and the person or persons in charge of the vehicle are
by reason of physical injury incapacitated to such an extent as to be unable to
provide for its custody or removal.
      (3)   When any vehicle is left unattended upon a street and is so parked
illegally as to constitute a definite hazard or obstruction to the normal
movement of traffic, or is parked in violation of the night parking
restrictions set forth in § 73.02.
   (B)   Whenever an officer removes a vehicle from a street as authorized in
this section and the officer knows or is able to ascertain from the
registration records in the vehicle the name and address of the owner thereof,
the officer shall immediately give or cause to be given notice in writing to
the owner of the fact of the removal and the reasons therefor and of the place
to which the vehicle has been removed. In the event any such vehicle is stored
in a public garage, a copy of the notice shall be given to the proprietor of
the garage.
   (C)   The owner or operator of any such vehicle so towed in may regain
possession thereof by paying in full to the owner or operator of the garage
having possession of the vehicle the towage charges plus the storage charges
incurred pursuant to this section.
   (D)   All towage charges and storage charges incurred as herein provided
shall become a lien upon the vehicle in favor of the owner or operator of the
garage in possession of the vehicle. The owner or operator of the garage as
herein provided having a lien on any vehicle may after 60 days proceed to
foreclose on the lien in the same manner as provided for the foreclosure of
mechanics' liens.
('79 Code, § 8-29)
Statutory reference:
   Foreclosure proceeding for mechanics' liens, see I.C. 32-33-9
   Liens on motor vehicles for storage, see I.C. 32-33-10
BUSES; TAXICABS
§ 72.15 STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING BUSES.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the operator of a common carrier bus to stand
or park such vehicle upon any street at any place other than a bus stand.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for the operator of a common carrier bus to stop
such vehicle upon any street at any place for the purpose of loading or
unloading passengers or their baggage other than at a bus stop, bus stand, or
passenger loading zone so designated as provided herein, except in case of an
emergency.
   (C)   The operator of a common carrier bus shall enter a bus stop, bus
stand, or passenger loading zone on a public street in such a manner that the
bus when stopped to load or unload passengers or baggage shall be in a position
with the right front wheel of the vehicle not further than 18 inches from the
curb and the bus approximately parallel to the curb so as not to unduly impede
the movement of other vehicular traffic.
('79 Code, § 8-25) (Ord. 14-1997, passed 7-8-97)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 72.16 STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING OF TAXICABS.
   It shall be unlawful for the operator of a taxicab to stand or park such
vehicle upon any street at any place other than in a taxicab stand; provided,
however, that this provision shall not prevent the operator of a taxicab from
temporarily stopping in accordance with other stopping or parking regulations
at any place while actually engaged in the expeditious loading or unloading
passengers.
('79 Code, § 8-26)
Penalty, see § 10.99
HANDICAPPED PARKING SPACES
§ 72.20 APPLICATION.
   The provisions of this chapter are enforceable on all parking facilities,
subject to the provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-1 et seq., regardless of whether the
parking facility is privately or publicly owned.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.21 AUTHORITY OF POLICE.
   City personnel, designated by the Chief of Police, and the officers of the
Police Department shall have the authority to issue citations of violation of
the parking provisions of this chapter, addressing accessible parking spaces
for persons with a physical challenge.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.22 PARKING FEES AND FINES.
   A $50 fine shall be imposed for the first violation in a calendar year in
the parking spaces reserved for persons with a physical challenge. If the
violator fails to pay the fine within seven business days of the violation, he
or she shall pay an additional $50 as a late penalty; such payment shall not
eliminate or replace the parking fine owed.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.23 DEFINITIONS.
   As used in this subchapter:
   MOTOR VEHICLE. Has the meaning set forth at I.C. 9-13-2-105.
   PARKING FACILITY. Any facility or combination of facilities for motor
vehicle parking that contains parking spaces for the public, whether publicly
or privately owned.
   PERSON WITH A PHYSICAL CHALLENGE. A person who has been issued a placard
under the I.C. 9-14-5, or a person with a registration plate for a motor
vehicle for persons with a physical challenge issued by the Bureau of Motor
Vehicles under I.C. 9-18-22.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
Editor’s notes:
   I.C. 9-14-5 was repealed by P.L. 198-2016, Sec. 185.
   I.C. 9-18-22 was added by P.L. 2-1991, Sec. 6 and expired 12-31-2016 by P.L.
198-2016, Sec. 262.
§ 72.24 PARKING FOR PERSONS WITH A PHYSICAL CHALLENGE REQUIRED.
   (A)   The owner of any parking facility shall provide accessible parking for
persons with a physical challenge. The number of accessible spaces so provided
shall, as a minimum, comply with the provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-2.
   (B)   The city shall reserve parking spaces on municipally owned lots as
prescribed by state law. The number of accessible spaces so provided shall, as
a minimum, comply with provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-2. In addition, the city shall
reserve parking on city streets as required to be used for the exclusive use of
persons with a physical challenge.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.25 PARKING FOR PERSONS WITH A PHYSICAL CHALLENGE.
   (A)   Only vehicles displaying a placard on the dashboard or rearview
mirror, as issued by the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles, or any successor
agency thereof, or displaying a registration plate for persons with a physical
challenge, may make use of the marked spaces pursuant to this section. Persons
utilizing the spaces must obey all other regulations and restrictions effective
in that zone.
   (B)   Parking of a vehicle by any person in a space designated hereunder,
without a visible placard or registration plate for persons with a physical
challenge showing such parking to be authorized, shall be unlawful, and shall
subject the owner and driver of the vehicle so parked to the penalties provided
for violators in this code.
   (C)   The Board of Public Works and Safety shall be empowered to establish
and so designate accessible parking spaces at such places, and in such numbers
that the designation shall comply with the requirements of the Americans with
Disabilities Act at all city on-street and off-street parking facilities.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.26 COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW REQUIRED.
   The manner of posting notice parking spaces for persons with a physical
challenge, and the size and location of parking spaces, shall comply with
provisions of the I.C. 5-16-92 and I.C. 5-16-9-4.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.27 EXCLUSIVENESS OF STATE PARKING PERMITS.
   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to require a person to obtain or
display any permit, registration plate, or registration decal other than those
specified in I.C. 5-16-9-9(c) in order to stand or park in a space reserved for
persons with a physical challenge, as established pursuant to I.C. 5-16-9-1 et
seq. or this chapter.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.28 RECIPROCITY.
   As required by I.C. 5-16-9-9(d), a motor vehicle displaying an unexpired
parking permit for a person with a physical challenge, an unexpired physically
challenged veteran’s registration plate, or an unexpired registration plate or
decal for persons with a physical challenge issued under the laws of another
state, shall be permitted to stand or park in a space reserved for a person
with a physical challenge, but only when the vehicle is being used to transport
a person with a physical challenge.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.29 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The provisions of §
72.30(A) through (C) may be enforced as follows:
      (1)   The violator may be issued a citation for the commission of a Class
C infraction pursuant to the provisions of the I.C. 5-16-9-5 of the state
statute concerning parking facilities for persons with a physical challenge; or
      (2)   The violator may be issued a citation for the violation of the
local ordinance herein established.
   (B)   The provisions of §
72.30(D) shall be enforced through the issuance of a citation for violation of
the local ordinance herein established.
   (C)   The Police Department, or any officers of the Police Department, shall
have the responsibility for citing violations of §
72.30(A) through (C).
   (D)   The chief code enforcement officer shall have the primary
responsibility for citing violations of §
72.30(D).
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.30 VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Any person who parks a motor vehicle that does not have displayed a
valid and unexpired registration plate, placard or decal for a physically
challenged person or a physically challenged veteran, issued under the laws of
the State of Indiana or under the laws of another state, in a parking space
reserved under this chapter for a vehicle for a person with a physical
challenge, shall be deemed to be in violation of this chapter.
   (B)   Any person who knowingly parks in a parking space reserved for a
person with a physical challenge, while displaying a placard, decal or
registration plate to which neither the person or the person’s passenger is
entitled, shall be deemed to be in violation of this chapter.
   (C)   Any person who displays for use in parking in a reserved space for the
physically challenged, a placard or license plate not issued under the laws of
the State of Indiana or some other state, shall be deemed in violation of this
chapter.
   (D)   Any owner of a parking facility, who fails to comply with the
provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-1 et seq. relating to accessible parking spaces for
the physically challenged, shall be deemed in violation of this chapter. For
the purpose of this division, notice of an ordinance violation shall be deemed
given to the owner of the parking facility when served upon the local agent in
charge of the operation of the parking facility. Pursuant to the provisions of
I.C. 36-1-6-2, before any action to enforce compliance with the provisions of
this chapter is brought under this division, all persons holding a substantial
interest in the property shall be given 90 days to bring the property into full
compliance.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.31 PENALTY.
   (A)   In any action brought for a violation under this chapter, whoever
violates the provisions of §
72.30 shall be subject to penalties under §
10.99.
   (B)   Nothing in division (A) of this section shall be construed as
preventing the enforcement of parking violations for the physically challenged
pursuant to the provisions of the I.C. 5-16-9-5.
   (C)   Any person found in violation of §
72.30 who fails to provide required accessible parking spaces for persons with
a physical challenge, after having been given 90 days to do so, shall be
subject to penalties under §
10.99. Each day that the failure to bring the parking facility into compliance
with the provisions of this chapter and state statute continues shall be
considered a separate offense.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
§ 72.32 SUPREMACY CLAUSE.
   The provisions of this chapter are intended as being supplemental to, and
not in replacement of, the provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-1 et seq. Should a
conflict be found to exist, the provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-1 shall be deemed as
controlling. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as limiting the
enforcement of the provisions of I.C. 5-16-9-1 et seq. as therein provided.
(Ord. 08-2018, passed 6-26-18)
CHAPTER 73: BICYCLES AND TOY VEHICLES
Section
Bicycles
   
73.01   Manner of riding bicycles on sidewalks
   
73.02   Use of bicycle paths
   
73.03   Parking of bicycles
   
73.04   Impoundment of bicycles
Statutory reference:
   Authority to regulate bicycles, see 9-21-1-3(a)(9)
BICYCLES
§ 73.01 MANNER OF RIDING BICYCLES ON SIDEWALKS.
   (A)   Whenever a person is riding a bicycle upon a sidewalk that person
shall yield the right-of-way to any pedestrian and shall give audible signal
before overtaking and passing the pedestrian.
   (B)   On Main Street, between Sixth Street and Ninth Street no person shall
ride a bicycle, roller skates, inline skates, or skateboard upon a sidewalk;
operators in such areas shall walk bicycles while traveling on sidewalks.
Violations of this section shall result in the forfeiture to the Police
Department of the bicycle, roller skates, inline skates, or skateboard involved
for not less than seven days or more than 14 days.
('79 Code, § 8-16) (Ord. 656, passed 5-25-76; Am. Ord. 09-1996, passed 6-25-96)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 73.02 USE OF BICYCLE PATHS.
   Whenever a usable path for bicycles has been provided adjacent to a roadway,
it shall be unlawful for a bicycle rider to fail to use the path.
('79 Code, § 8-17)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 73.03 PARKING OF BICYCLES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to park a bicycle upon a street other
than upon the roadway against the curb or upon the sidewalk in a rack to
support the bicycle or against a building or at the curb, in such manner as to
afford the least obstruction to pedestrian traffic.
('79 Code, § 8-18)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 73.04 IMPOUNDMENT OF BICYCLES.
   In addition to any other penalty provided by law, any person who violates
any of the provisions of this subchapter while on a bicycle may, upon
conviction have his bicycle impounded for a period not to exceed 30 days.
('79 Code, § 8-30)
CHAPTER 74: RAILROADS
Section
   
74.01   Blocking railroad crossings
   
74.02   Manner of blocking
§ 74.01 BLOCKING RAILROAD CROSSINGS.
   It shall be unlawful for any standing train, engine or other equipment
operated by a railroad to block any railroad crossing for a period of time
exceeding five minutes; provided, however, that the provisions of this section
shall not apply to passenger trains, moving trains, or in cases of an extreme
emergency.
('79 Code, § 13-2)
Penalty, see § 70.99
§ 74.02 MANNER OF BLOCKING.
   It shall be the duty of the crew of each railroad train, engine or other
rail equipment to allow traffic to pass over a railroad crossing in such a
manner and for such time as to cause the least delay and interruption for the
smooth flow of traffic after each blocking of the crossing.
('79 Code, § 13-3)
Penalty, see § 70.99
CHAPTER 75: TRAFFIC SCHEDULES

SCHEDULE VI. BUSINESS PARKING DISTRICT.
   (A)   Business Parking District defined. That area of parking spaces between
the intersections of 5th Street and Main Street to 9th Street and Main Street,
on both sides of Main Street and for one-half block either side of Main Street
shall constitute the Business Parking District, except for those parking spaces
bordering the Fulton County Courthouse square.
   (B)   Permitted parking. Parking in the Business Parking District is
permitted for customers and clients of downtown businesses, including business
deliveries and pickups, and business visitations.
   (C)   Prohibited parking. It is a violation of this schedule to park in any
parking space within the Business Parking District between the hours of 7:00
a.m., and 8:00 p.m., and to be:
      (1)   An employee of any business located within the Business Parking
District, parked while during the hours of employment; or
      (2)   A resident of any apartment or residential property within the
Business Parking District, unless the resident is engaging in a business
transaction in a building other than the location of the resident’s residence.
   (D)   Penalties for violation.
      (1)   Any person who shall be found to violate this schedule shall be
subject to a fine of $25 per occurrence, plus all costs through the Ordinance
Bureau, or court.
      (2)   Any vehicle found in violation of this schedule on three or more
occasions, or in violation of Chapter 76 Parking Schedules, shall be impounded
and towed at the violator’s expense.
      (3)   Any vehicle towed under this schedule’s penalty provision may be
recovered upon payment of all penalties, towing and storage fees due by the
owner of the vehicle.
(Ord. 03-2009, passed 5-12-09)
CHAPTER 77: GOLF CART USE AND REGULATION
Section
   
77.01   Definitions
   
77.02   Intent
   
77.03   Minimum safety equipment
   
77.04   Registration and inspection
   
77.05   Financial responsibility
   
77.06   General regulations
 
   
77.99   Penalty
§ 77.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purposes of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid current license to operate a motor vehicle issued
by the State of Indiana or any other state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability coverage applicable to the golf cart and
compliant with all Indiana laws applicable to a motor vehicle operated on the
public highway of the State of Indiana.
   GOLF CART. Shall have the definition provided by I.C. 9-13-2-69.7. As it now
exists, the term means: a four wheeled motor vehicle originally and
specifically designed and intended to transport one or more individuals and
golf clubs for the purpose of playing the game of golf on a golf course.
   OPERATOR. A person(s) holding a valid driver’s license issued by the State
of Indiana or another state.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23)
§ 77.02 INTENT.
   It is the intent of this chapter to allow for the use of golf carts on the
local streets within the city. To ensure public safety and welfare, the
operation of golf carts must comply with certain vehicle regulations. The
operation of a golf cart on city streets is strictly prohibited unless the golf
cart is operated and equipped in full compliance with this chapter.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23) Penalty, see §
77.99
§ 77.03 MINIMUM SAFETY EQUIPMENT.
   (A)   All golf carts operated on city streets shall have the following
minimum safety equipment:
      (1)   A rearview and sideview mirrors;
      (2)   A bright orange flag affixed to the rear of the golf cart that is a
minimum of six feet in height from the roadway;
      (3)   A slow moving vehicle sign that conforms to the provisions of I.C.
9-21-9-2, affixed to the rear of the golf cart;
      (4)   Brake lights and turn signals; and
      (5)   If operated after dark or before dawn, headlights and taillights.
      (6)   A flashing light, at the highest point of the vehicle, on at all
times (day or night).
   (B)   All of the minimum safety equipment described above shall be
functional, and in use at all times while the golf cart is in operation on city
streets.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23) Penalty, see §
77.99
§ 77.04 REGISTRATION AND INSPECTION.
   (A)   No golf cart shall be operated on any city street unless it is
registered.
   (B)   Owners of a golf cart who wish to operate it on city streets must
register the golf cart with the Rochester Police Department. The golf cart
shall undergo an initial inspection with the Rochester Police Department to
determine compliance with this chapter and proof of financial responsibility
prior to registration. Once the golf cart passes inspection, it may be
registered.
   (C)   The annual registration fee for golf carts shall be $100. The
registration, upon issuance, shall be valid for the calendar year with each
registration issued expiring December 31, of each year.
   (D)   The Rochester Police Department is directed to develop and utilize a
registration form. Such form shall contain a certification that the operator
will observe all traffic laws applicable to the operation of a motor vehicle.
The Rochester Police Department shall handle the ordering of all permit
stickers and collection of all registration fees. Registration fees shall be
placed in the City Ordinance Fund and the Rochester Police Department shall
receive all funds derived from the registration of golf carts.
   (E)   The City of Rochester Board of Public Works and Safety may provide an
exception to the registration requirements of this chapter for good cause.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23) Penalty, see §
77.99
§ 77.05 FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY.
   All golf carts to be operated and used on city streets shall be insured.
Proof of financial responsibility shall be in accordance with I.C. 9-25-4-4. A
person who operates a golf cart on the city streets shall at all times maintain
the state required minimum amount of financial responsibility for the operation
of said golf cart. Proof of financial responsibility shall be carried on the
golf cart or operator at all times.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23) Penalty, see §
77.99
§ 77.06 GENERAL REGULATIONS.
   (A)   Golf carts are prohibited from operating on any part of Main Street,
or any state road or highway with the exception of crossing the roadway at a
perpendicular angle. This prohibition includes all of Main Street, 9th Street
east of Main Street, 18th Street west of Main Street, and any part of State
Road 25 and State Road 14.
   (B)   Golf carts shall not be operated on any sidewalk, pedestrian walkway,
multi-use path, jogging path, greenway, or trail, except to cross at
intersections in a path perpendicular to the path or walkway.
   (C)   Only persons holding a valid driver’s license may operate a golf cart
on city streets. The operator must possess a valid driver’s license on their
person at all times operating the golf cart.
   (D)   The maximum occupancy of a golf cart traveling on city streets shall
be one person per bucket seat and three persons per bench seat. All persons
riding the golf cart must be seated in one of the manufacturer-designed seats,
and may not be standing or riding on the back on in any place designated for
cargo or sporting equipment. All passengers must be seated at all times.
   (E)   Golf carts must be operated in compliance with all applicable local
and state traffic laws, and the operator may be ticketed in the same manner as
motor vehicle operators.
   (F)   Golf carts may park in any public vehicle parking space in adherence
with all rules and regulations relating to the parking of vehicles. Golf carts
may be parked in private driveways and private areas designated for vehicle
parking with the permission of the property owner.
   (G)   Golf carts may not be parked or stored on a road, street, alley or
thoroughfare overnight.
   (H)   Golf carts shall not be operated on city streets during inclement
weather or when visibility is impaired by weather, smoke, fog, or other
conditions.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23) Penalty, see §
77.99
§ 77.07 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any violation of the provisions of this chapter or a failure to comply
with any of its requirements shall subject the offender to a penalty as
follows:
      (1)   First offense - $100;
      (2)   Second offense $250;
      (3)   Third offense - $500 and revocation of registration. Registration
revocation will be in effect for a minimum of one year.
   (B)   In addition to fees, if public safety requires, the golf cart may be
towed at the owner’s expense.
   (C)   Each day of violating this chapter shall be construed as a separate
violation.
   (D)   All fines collected pursuant to this section shall be deposited in the
general fund of the city.
(Ord. 02-2023, passed 5-23-23)

CHAPTER 90: ABANDONED, NUISANCE AND JUNKED MOTOR VEHICLES
Section

Statutory reference:
   Abandoned motor vehicles, see 9-22-1-1 et seq.
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   JUNK CAR. Any motor vehicle which:
      (1)   Shall be an “abandoned vehicle” as that term is defined in I.C. 9-
13-2-1;
      (2)   Does not bear a currently valid license plate, and is located
either on public property or on private property in a location visible from
public property and not in a garage or other building for a period of 30 days;
or
      (3)   Has the engine, transmission, differential, wheels or any other
operating component removed or disabled so as to make the vehicle inoperable
and which is located either on public property or on private property in a
place visible from public property and not in a garage or other building for a
period of 30 days.
('79 Code, § 8-77) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69; Am. Ord. 7-1989, passed 2-28-89)
§ 90.02 NUISANCE DECLARED.
   All junk cars are declared to be nuisances; provided, however, that no such
car shall be a nuisance if it is located in a lawfully operated junkyard
awaiting permission for junking from the State Bureau of Motor Vehicles, or if
it is in the possession of lawfully licensed automobile dealer and at his
legally recognized place of business or such other lots properly zoned for such
purpose.
('79 Code, § 8-78) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
Cross-reference:
   
Nuisances, see Ch. 94
REMOVAL
§ 90.15 REQUIRED.
   All junk cars shall be removed within ten days after the service of the
notice required by §
90.17 by the owner of the car or the owner or occupant of the real estate upon
which it is located.
('79 Code, § 8-79) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
Statutory reference:
   Removal of vehicles by local officials, see I.C.9-22-1-1 et seq.
§ 90.16 ORDER OF REMOVAL.
   Any member of the Police Department may order the removal of a junk car.
('79 Code, § 8-80) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
§ 90.17 NOTICE.
   When any member of the Police Department orders that a junk car be removed,
a notice of the order shall be placed upon the car and copies of it shall be
served upon any adult occupying the real estate on which it is located and upon
the owner of the car, if they are known. If no occupant of the real estate or
owner of the junk car can be found, then such notice may be affixed to any
building on the real estate on which the car is located; if there is no
building on the real estate, then the notice may be affixed elsewhere on the
real estate.
('79 Code, § 8-81) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
Statutory reference:
   Notice tag prepared by police officer, see I.C. 19-22-1-1 et seq.
§ 90.18 REMOVAL BY CITY.
   If a junk car is not removed within ten days after the service of the notice
required by §
90.17, then the Police Department may cause it to be removed at the expense of
the owner of the real estate or of the owner of the junk car.
('79 Code, § 8-82) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
§ 90.19 IMPOUNDMENT.  
   All junk cars which are removed by the city pursuant to the provisions of
this chapter shall be impounded.
('79 Code, § 8-83)
Cross-reference:
   
Impoundment of vehicles, see § 71.05
§ 90.20 REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED CAR.
   Within 30 days of the impoundment of a junk car pursuant to the provisions
of this chapter, its owner may repossess it if he pays all expenses incurred in
its towing, impoundment and storage.
('79 Code, § 8-84) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
§ 90.21 SALE OF UNCLAIMED VEHICLE.
   If a junk car is not repossessed by its owner within 30 days of its
impoundment, the Police Department shall sell it to the highest bidder at a
public auction which shall be held no later than ten days after one publication
of a notice of such sale in a newspaper of general circulation in the city.
('79 Code, § 8-85) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
§ 90.22 USE OF SALE PROCEEDS.
   All proceeds from the sale of a junk vehicle pursuant to this chapter shall
be used to defray the expenses incurred in removing and impounding the vehicle.
('79 Code, § 8-86) (Ord. 455, passed 3-25-69)
Statutory reference:
   Use of sale proceeds, see I.C. 9-22-1-26 and 9-22-1-27
§ 90.23 TOWING AND STORAGE CHARGES.
   The City Council shall establish by ordinance the charges allowed for towing
and storage of abandoned vehicles, which shall be filed with the bureau of
motor vehicles and shall be available for public inspection at the office of
the city clerk.

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 91.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL. Any living creature domestic or wild, except human beings.
   ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER. Any person or persons designated by the Fulton
County Commissioners or law enforcement officer who is qualified to perform
such duties under the authority of this chapter and the state.
   ANIMAL SHELTER. A facility for the purpose of impounding and/or caring for
animals held under the authority of this chapter or state law.
   KENNEL. A place primarily for keeping four or more adult dogs or other small
animals that are ordinarily bred for sale as pets. Also could include temporary
care facility for compensation. Includes any premises where in any person
engages in the business of boarding, breeding, buying, letting for hire,
training for a fee, or selling dogs and cats.
   OWNER. Any person, partnership or corporation owning, keeping or harboring
one or more animals. An animal shall be deemed to be owned if kept or harbored,
fed or sheltered for three consecutive days or more.
   PERSON. Any individual, partnership, company or corporation.
   PET. Any animal kept for pleasure rather than utility.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE. Any animal or animals which:
      (1)   Molests passersby or passing vehicles;
      (2)   Attacks other animals;
      (3)   Trespasses on school grounds;
      (4)   Is repeatedly at large or unrestrained;
      (5)   Damages private or public property;
      (6)   Barks, whines or howls in an excessive, continuous or untimely
fashion.
   RESTRAINT. Any animal secured by a leash or lead, or under the control of a
responsible person and obedient to that person's commands, or within the real
property limits of its owner.
('79 Code, § 3-1) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00;
Am. Ord. 12-2008, passed 11-25-08)
§ 91.02 MANNER OF KEEPING.
   (A)   The keeping of dogs, cats and other animals shall be done in such a
manner as to be conducive to the health and safety of such animals, and to
safeguard the health, peace and decency of the public.
   (B)   All animals shall be kept under restraint at all times.
   (C)   No owner shall fail to prevent his or her animals from molesting
passersby, chasing vehicles, obstructing traffic, attacking other animals or
people, trespassing onto school grounds, or trespassing onto private or public
property in such a manner as to damage or defecate on such property.
   (D)   No owner shall fail to confine a female dog in heat within a building,
veterinary hospital or boarding kennel in such a manner that the female cannot
come into contact with male dogs except for planned breeding. The confinement
of the female shall be maintained at all times during the heat period.
   (E)   Unrestrained and public nuisance animals, abandoned animals, animals
found suffering from cruelty or lack of care as specified in this chapter,
animals used or abused in any manner prohibited by this chapter, may be seized
by the animal control officer or any law enforcement officer from any place,
public or private and impounded at the animal shelter. The owner may also be
proceeded against for violation of this chapter.
   (F)   All waste from animals shall be disposed of properly. Waste shall be
confined to the owner’s property. Any animal waste on public property by the
animal is the owner’s responsibility to clean up, excepting a disabled person
working with a service animal. This provision applies to owners of horses
lawfully used for transportation, who may meet this requirement through use of
a device reasonably designed to catch manure and prevent its deposit onto city
streets.
   (G)   Individual homes shall not harbor more than three dogs and not more
than five total animals per household without registering for a special permit
from the City Council. Each time an addition is made to the number of animals,
the City Council shall be notified by certified letter. Fish shall be exempt
from this requirement. Small mammals, birds, amphibians and reptiles (less than
one pound) are also exempt from this requirement.
   (H)   If by a license tag or other means the owner of an impounded animal
can be identified, the animal control officer, police officer or any employee
of a law enforcement agency shall immediately contact the owner by phone or
mail.
(‘79 Code, § 3-2) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00;
Am. Ord. 12-2008, passed 11-25-08; Am. Ord. 02-2015, passed 1-27-15) Penalty,
see §
91.99
§ 91.03 ANIMAL TREATMENT; CARE AND CRUELTY
   (A)   Every owner of an animal within the city shall:
      (1)   Keep such animal in a clean, sanitary and healthy area. No animal
shall be confined in an area so as to be forced to stand, sit or lie in its own
excreta.
      (2)   Not confine an animal in an area littered with debris or any other
obstacles which would impair, prohibit or reduce the animal's movement or cause
injury within such area of confinement.
      (3)   Confine his or her animals in an area of sufficient size to permit
such animals to exercise and move about.
      (4)   Not prevent in any way any animal from seeking proper shelter by
chaining, roping or fencing in any animal.
      (5)   Not tether a dog by a choker collar, or on a chain or similar means
of restraint less than ten feet in length or of such weight as to prevent such
animal from moving about or causing injury to such animal.
      (6)   Not fail to provide his or her animals with sufficient, wholesome
food and clean water.
      (7)   Not fail to provide his or her animal with proper, soundly and
effectively constructed shelter and protection from varying elements of the
weather at all times.
      (8)   Not fail to provide humane and veterinary care and counsel for
sick, injured or diseased animals and shall segregate such animals from the
healthy so as to prevent transmittal of any sickness or disease.
   (B)   No person shall beat, cruelly ill treat, torment, overload, overwork,
or otherwise abuse or mistreat any animal.
   (C)   No person shall injure or cause to be injured any animal by means of
any motor vehicle, firearm, or any other instrument or object and fail to
immediately report the existence, location, description and tag number, if any,
of the injured animal to the humane society and in doing so give his or her
name and address.
   (D)   No person shall abandon any animal on any place public or private,
including any public or private highway, or road, or upon the property of
another.
   (E)   No person shall keep or use any animal for the purpose of fighting or
cause or permit any fighting or other combat between animals. No person shall
be a party to or be present as a spectator to any such fighting or other combat
between animals. No person shall knowingly suffer or permit the use of any
building, yard, ground or any other premises belonging to any person for any
fighting or other combat between animals; and no person shall carry, haul or
deliver any animal for the aforementioned purposes.
   (F)   No person shall expose any known poisonous substance, whether mixed
with food or not, so that the substance shall be liable to be consumed by any
animal.
   (G)   It shall not be considered a violation of this section for the owner
of a golf course, or its employees or agents, to take the actions prescribed in
§
130.04(E) concerning the discharge of firearms at nuisance animals.
(‘79 Code, § 3-3) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00;
Am. Ord. 06-2014, passed 6-3-14) Penalty, see §
91.99
Statutory reference:
   Animal cruelty, see I.C. 35-46-3-7 through 35-46-3-12
§ 91.04 HARBORING NOISY ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor any animal which
disturbs the peace by making loud noises.
('79 Code, § 3-4)
Penalty, see § 91.99
Cross-reference:
   Noise, see
Ch. 94
§ 91.05 BITE CASES AND QUARANTINE.
   (A)   Any animal which bites a person shall be immediately, securely
confined and quarantined for a minimum period of ten days. The animal may be
quarantined on the owner's premises or in a facility of the owner’s choice at
the owner's expense, or impounded at the county facility.
   (B)   Any owner whose animal has bitten a person and keeps such animal on
their property shall:
      (1)   Securely confine such animal at all times during the quarantine
period.
      (2)   Pay any and all fees for the pathological examination of the animal
for rabies and any and all fees for boarding, shipping or other related
expenses.
   (C)   Any owner reclaiming an animal placed under quarantine shall provide
proof of rabies vaccination.
   (D)   Any person who refuses or fails to comply with the procedures and
requirements for the quarantining of their animal shall surrender such animal
to any animal control officer or law enforcement officer upon demand and may
also be proceeded against for violation of this subchapter.
(‘79 Code, § 3-5) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00;
Am. Ord. 04-2015, passed 1-27-15) Penalty, see §
91.99
IMPOUNDMENT
§ 91.15 NOTICE OF IMPOUNDMENT.
   Written notice of the fact of impoundment under the provisions of this
chapter shall be served upon the owner or keeper of any animal which is so
impounded.
('79 Code, § 3-18) (Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
§ 91.16 REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED ANIMAL; PROOF OF OWNERSHIP, PAYMENT OF FINE
REQUIRED.
   Any person claiming an impounded animal shall upon request of the humane
officer provide proof of ownership by means of a rabies certificate of such
animal and pay all applicable fines and fees before such animal shall be
released.
('79 Code, § 3-20) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-
00)
§ 91.17 DISPOSITION OF UNCLAIMED ANIMALS.
   Any animal not reclaimed by its owner within three working days of
impoundment shall become the property of the animal shelter and shall be
disposed of at the discretion of the animal shelter in one of the following
manners:
   (A)   Euthanasia, using a method approved by the animal shelter.
   (B)   Release for adoption, to a new owner who shows evidence and intention
to provide the animal with humane care and abide by all laws governing animal
control and welfare.
   (C)   Release to the environment. Whenever possible wildlife shall be
relocated to their natural habitat. Wildlife shall be exempt from the three-day
holding requirement, thereby permitting immediate release.
('79 Code, § 3-24) (Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
§ 91.18 LOST OR STRAY ANIMALS.
   (A)   Persons finding a stray animal are to notify the animal control
officer within 48 hours. At the discretion of the animal control officer, the
animal may be kept by the finder and a found report left with the animal
control officer, to enable the finder an opportunity to return the animal to
its rightful owner.
   (B)   Any found animal may be surrendered to the animal control officer to
be held at the animal shelter for three working days, before a disposition is
made. Any animal not claimed within the three day period shall become the
properly of the animal shelter and shall be disposed of as set forth in §
91.17.
   (C)   Persons finding an animal are obligated to comply with all rules and
regulations of this chapter pertaining to humane care and treatment of animals,
while said animal is in their custody awaiting return to its actual owner.
   (D)   With the exception of the animal control officer, the finder will be
considered the found animal's owner for the purposes of this subchapter only
after the animal is in the finder's custody for 30 continuous days.
(Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
§ 91.19 FURTHER REQUIREMENTS.
   All other adoption requirements and fees shall be at the discretion of the
animal shelter.
('79 Code, § 3-26) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-
00)
DOGS AND CATS
§ 91.35 RABIES VACCINATION REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor any dog which is over the age
of three months which is not immunized against rabies at least once each year.
('79 Code, § 3-37) (Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
§ 91.36 EMERGENCY PROCLAMATION BY MAYOR; VIOLATION.
   (A)   Whenever the Mayor apprehends that there is danger of the existence or
spread of any dangerous disease relating to dogs, he shall issue a
proclamation, ordering and requiring all persons owning, possession or
harboring any member of the canine family to confine or muzzle said animal for
a term of not less than 30 days, nor more than 90 days following the date of
such proclamation.
   (B)   Any dog found in violation of the provisions of such proclamation
shall be destroyed on order of the Chief of Police.
('79 Code, § 3-38)
§ 91.37 CONFINEMENT OF DOGS KEPT FOR COMMERCIAL BREEDING.
   All female dogs kept for commercial breeding shall be kept housed during
their breeding period and shall not be allowed out of doors during such period.
('79 Code, § 3-39)
§ 91.38 (RESERVED).
§ 91.39 CONFINEMENT OF CATS KEPT FOR COMMERCIAL BREEDING.
   All female cats which are kept for commercial breeding purposes shall be
kept housed during their breeding period and shall not be allowed outside
during this period.
('79 Code, § 3-64 ) (Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
OTHER ANIMALS
§ 91.70 EXOTIC AND DANGEROUS ANIMALS.
   No exotic, venomous or dangerous animal may be owned or housed within the
city limits. Dangerous animals include, but are not limited to, non-
domesticated cats, canines, bears, etc.
(Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
§ 91.71 DANGEROUS ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   Ownership or possession prohibited. No person shall own, keep, or
harbor a dangerous animal within the city; provided, this section shall not
apply to animals under the control of a law enforcement or military agency. For
the purpose of this chapter, an animal may be declared dangerous by the animal
control officer, police officer or any officers of a law enforcement agency, if
the animal exhibits vicious behavior in present or past conduct, including but
not limited to:
      (1)   (a)   Evidence that the animal has, without provocation, bitten or
attacked a person and/or animals three times in a consecutive 12-month period;
or
         (b)   Did bite or attack, once causing wound or injuries creating a
potential danger to the health or life of the victim; or
         (c)   Could not be controlled or restrained at the time of a bite or
attack upon an animal or person; and
   
      (2)   That in order to preserve the public health, safety and welfare of
the community, the destruction of said animal is necessary.
   (B)   Determination and appeals procedure.  Whenever an animal is declared
dangerous, the animal control officer shall notify the animal's owner or
custodian of the declaration and the animal control officer's intent to
euthanize the animal unless the determination is timely appealed hereunder.
Notice of the declaration shall be served either in person or by certified or
registered mail. The animal, if not already held in quarantine, shall be
surrendered to the animal control officer.
      (1)   Any decision of the animal control officer under the provisions of
these divisions may be appealed to the Board of Public Works and Safety. The
appeal of the owner to the Board shall be in writing and be filed with the
Board of Public Works and Safety within ten days after receipt of notification
from the animal control officer that said animal has been found to be
dangerous. The disposition of any animal shall be stayed during the pendency of
such appeal. The animal shall remain in the custody of the animal control
officer during the appeal process.
      (2)   Upon receipt of a written appeal, the Board shall provide notice
and conduct an adjudicative hearing in accordance with the terms of I.C. 4-21.5
et seq. Thereafter, the Board shall render a decision that said animal is
dangerous and must be euthanized, or is not dangerous and should be returned to
the owner. The decision of the Board shall be final and binding upon the city
and upon the appellant. This decision may be appealed according to the
provisions of I.C. 4-21.5-5-1 et seq.
   (C)   Costs. The owners of any animal which is impounded and/or euthanized
under this section shall be held responsible for payment of any expenses so
incurred by the animal control officer, and failure to pay such fee to the
Department within 15 days after destruction of such animal shall constitute a
violation of the chapter.
(Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
§ 91.72 FARM ANIMAL AND FOWL.
   No farm animal or fowl may be owned or housed within the city limits.
(Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)
Penalty, see § 91.99
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any owner reclaiming an impounded animal shall pay a fee set by the
Fulton County Ordinance No. 032100, § 1-003 and paid through Fulton County.
   (B)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter is subject to fines
set out in the Violations Bureau Ordinance.
('79 Code, § 3-6) (Ord. 768, passed 7-10-79; Am. Ord. 26-2000, passed 11-28-00)

AND PROTECTION

§ 92.01 OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the open burning of any
matter or material within the city limits, with the following exceptions:
   (A)   Residents of the city may burn charcoal and/or wood in outdoor
fireplaces and grills provided that the fireplaces or grills shall be placed in
such a location as to be reasonably removed from any neighboring residence so
as to avoid any smoke or fumes therefrom becoming a nuisance for any adjacent
neighbor.
   (B)   In the event that there are such unusual circumstances as to make the
burning of a substantial amount of combustible matter desirable, any person
wishing to burn any such material shall apply to the Clerk-Treasurer for
permission to burn such combustible material. Any such applications shall be
considered by the Board of Public Works and Safety and if authorized by them
any such burning will be done under the supervision of the City Fire
Department.
('79 Code, § 5-1) (Ord. 538, passed 5-23-72; Am. Ord. 56-1986, passed 7-8-86)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 92.02 RESIDENTIAL STORAGE OF CERTAIN INFLAMMABLE AND EXPLOSIVE LIQUIDS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to store any inflammable or explosive
liquids, other than that used for heating and cooking purposes, such as fuel
oil or liquefied petroleum gas in any area, if zoned as residential, other than
in approved, sealed containers or safety cans not exceeding an aggregate total
of five gallons.
('79 Code, § 5-3) (Ord. 450, passed 10-8-68)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 92.03 FALSE FIRE ALARMS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to give or attempt to give or cause to
be given a false fire alarm.
('79 Code, § 5-4)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 92.04 INTERFERENCE WITH FIRE HYDRANTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person who is not authorized by the Board of
Waterworks Trustees or the Superintendent of the Water Department willfully to
break, injure, open or in any other way interfere with any fire hydrant.
('79 Code, § 5-5)
Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 92.05 INSPECTIONS.
   The Chief of the Fire Department is empowered to at all times enter any
place that is kept, maintained or permitted to remain within the corporate
limits of the city, in such manner as to be a menace to the public safety from
fire, or to enter any such place as he has reasonable cause to believe contains
a menace to the public safety.
('79 Code, § 5-6)
§ 92.06 REMOVAL OF MENACES.
   (A)   The Chief of the Fire Department shall, when he has determined after
an examination that any place has become a menace to the public and safety by
reason of a danger of fire, immediately notify its owners or occupants to
remedy or remove such menace at once.
   (B)   At the same time the Chief shall make a report of such action to the
Board of Public Works and Safety and if the owner or occupant fails to remedy
or remove the menace, the Board of Public Works and Safety shall take the
actions authorized by state law.
('79 Code, § 5-7)
Penalty, see § 10.99
Statutory reference:
   Removal of unsafe buildings and structures, see I.C. 36-7-9-1 et seq.
§ 92.07 CONSUMER FIREWORKS.
   (A)   Consumer fire works shall only be used, ignited or discharged on the
following days and hours:
      (1)   Between the hours of 5:00 p.m. and two hours after sunset on June
29, June 30, July 1, July 2, July 3, July 5, July 6, July 7, July 8 and July 9;
      (2)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on July
4; and
      (3)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on
January 1.
   (B)   That consumer fireworks used, ignited or discharged on any other day
or hour except as specified in division (A) shall be a violation of this
section.
   (C)   A violation of this section may be written- against a person or
property owner.
      (1)   Person shall mean an individual, an association, an organization, a
limited liability company, or a corporation.
      (2)   Property owner shall mean any part owner, joint owner, tenant in
common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety of the
whole or part of a building, a structure or land.
   (D)   (1)   Any group or individual requesting the use of consumer fireworks
on days and hours other than those previously regulated shall obtain permission
from the Rochester Common Council at a publicly conducted meeting as required
by the Open Door Law.
      (2)   Upon receiving approval from the Common Council, the group or
individual shall pay to the Clerk-Treasurer a fee of $25, which shall be
deposited into the General Fund.
   (E)   Approval of the Common Council shall designate the specific dates and
hours the consumer fireworks may be used.
(Ord. 05-2008, passed 6-24-08; Am. Ord. 04-2009, passed 3-10-09)
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   That a violation of § 92.07 shall be subject to a fine in the amount
of $50 for the first offense, $100.00 for the second offense, and $300 for the
third offense.
   (B)   That fines for the first three offenses as described above shall be
paid to the Ordinance Violations Bureau.
   (C)   That a fourth offense or more may be filed within the county court of
jurisdiction and subject the offender to the maximum fine allowed by law for an
ordinance violation, and court costs.
(Ord. 05-2008, passed 6-24-08)
CHAPTER 93: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
93.01   Policy statement
   
93.02   Definitions

93.05   Discrimination in residential real estate-related transactions
